      <p><b>Hungary</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">Magyarország</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Hungarian" title="Help:IPA/Hungarian">[ˈmɒɟɒrorsaːɡ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hu-Magyarorsz%C3%A1g.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Hu-Magyarorsz%C3%A1g.ogg" class="internal" title="Hu-Magyarország.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is a country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Flaw_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flaw-2">[2]</a></sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> to the east and southeast, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> to the southwest, and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> to the west. Hungary covers an area of 93,030 square kilometres (35,920&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Basin" title="Pannonian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a>, with a population of 10&nbsp;million. <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Hungary" title="Languages of Hungary">official language</a>, is the world's most widely spoken <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic language</a>, and among the few non-<a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> widely spoken in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> is the country's capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_of_Hungary" title="List of cities and towns of Hungary">largest city</a>; other major urban areas include <a href="/wiki/Debrecen" title="Debrecen">Debrecen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Szeged" title="Szeged">Szeged</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miskolc" title="Miskolc">Miskolc</a>, <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9cs" title="Pécs">Pécs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gy%C5%91r" title="Győr">Győr</a>. </p>
      <p>The territory of present-day Hungary was for centuries inhabited by various peoples, including <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic people">Germanic tribes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avars</a>. The foundations of the Hungarian state were established in the late ninth century AD with the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_conquest_of_the_Carpathian_Basin" title="Hungarian conquest of the Carpathian Basin">conquest of the Carpathian Basin</a> by <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarian</a> grand prince <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d" title="Árpád">Árpád</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Acta_orientalia_Academiae_Scientiarum_Hungaricae_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Acta_orientalia_Academiae_Scientiarum_Hungaricae-16">[15]</a></sup> His great-grandson <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">Stephen I</a> ascended the throne in 1000, converting his realm to a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Christian kingdom</a>. By the 12th century, Hungary became a regional power, reaching its <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1301%E2%80%931526)" title="Kingdom of Hungary (1301–1526)">cultural and political height in the 15th century</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a> in 1526, it was partially <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Hungary" title="Ottoman Hungary">occupied by the Ottoman Empire</a> (1541–1699). Hungary came under <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg rule</a> at the turn of the 18th century, later <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1867" class="mw-redirect" title="Compromise of 1867">joining</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a> to form <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Major_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Major power">major power</a> into the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Austria-Hungary collapsed after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a> established Hungary's current borders, resulting in the loss of 71% of its territory, 58% of its population, and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">32% of ethnic Hungarians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Following the tumultuous <a href="/wiki/Hungary_between_the_World_Wars" title="Hungary between the World Wars">interwar period</a>, Hungary joined the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, suffering significant damage and casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-Montgomery_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thomas,_pg._11_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas,_pg._11-23">[22]</a></sup> Postwar Hungary became a <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite state</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, leading to the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic" title="Hungarian People's Republic">Hungarian People's Republic</a>. Following the failed <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">1956 revolution</a>, Hungary became a <a href="/wiki/Goulash_Communism" title="Goulash Communism">comparatively freer</a>, though still repressive, member of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Removal_of_Hungary%27s_border_fence_with_Austria" title="Removal of Hungary's border fence with Austria">removal of Hungary's border fence with Austria</a> accelerated the collapse of the Eastern Bloc, and <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Soviet_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Collapse of the Soviet government">subsequently the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> On 23 October 1989, Hungary became a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Hungary joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in 2004 and has been part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Hungary is a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> in international affairs, owing mostly to its <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Hungary" title="Culture of Hungary">cultural</a> and economic influence.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> It has a <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income economy</a> and ranks "very high" in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, with citizens enjoying <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Hungary" title="Healthcare in Hungary">universal health care</a> and tuition-free <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="List of universities in Hungary">secondary education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-europa_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa-29">[28]</a></sup> Hungary has a long history of significant contributions to <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_art" title="Hungarian art">arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Hungary" title="Music of Hungary">music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_literature" title="Hungarian literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary_at_the_Olympics" title="Hungary at the Olympics">sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Hungary" title="Science and technology in Hungary">science and technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannic_.=_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannic_.=-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">thirteenth-most popular</a> <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Hungary" title="Tourism in Hungary">tourist destination</a> in Europe, drawing 15.8 million international tourists in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-WTO_Tourism_Highlights_2016_Edition_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTO_Tourism_Highlights_2016_Edition-34">[33]</a></sup> It is a member of numerous international organisations, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Investment_Bank" title="International Investment Bank">IIB</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank" title="Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank">AIIB</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Hungary" title="Name of Hungary">Name of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The "H" in the name of Hungary (and Latin <i>Hungaria</i>) is most likely due to founded historical associations with the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, who had settled Hungary prior to the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>. The rest of the word comes from the Latinized form of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Greek" title="Medieval Greek">Byzantine Greek</a> <i>Oungroi</i> (Οὔγγροι). The Greek name was borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Bulgarian</a> <i>ągrinŭ</i>, in turn borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Oghur_languages" title="Oghur languages">Oghur-Turkic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Onogurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Onogurs">Onogur</a></i> ('ten [tribes of the] <a href="/wiki/Ogur" class="mw-redirect" title="Ogur">Ogurs</a>'). <i>Onogur</i> was the collective name for the tribes who later joined the <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgar</a> tribal confederacy that ruled the eastern parts of Hungary after the Avars.<sup id="cite_ref-Király_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Király-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a> is <i>Magyarország</i>, composed of <i>magyar</i> ('Hungarian') and <i>ország</i> ('country'). The name "Magyar", which refers to the people of the country, more accurately reflects the name of the country in some other languages such as <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> and other languages as <i>Magyaristan</i> or <i>Land of Magyars</i> or similar. The word <i>magyar</i> is taken from the name of one of the seven major semi-nomadic Hungarian tribes, <i>magyeri</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> The first element <i>magy</i> is likely from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Ugric" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Ugric">Proto-Ugric</a> *<i>mäńć-</i> 'man, person', also found in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Mansi_people" title="Mansi people">Mansi people</a> (<i>mäńćī, mańśi, måńś</i>). The second element <i>eri</i>, 'man, men, lineage', survives in Hungarian <i>férj</i> 'husband', and is cognate with <a href="/wiki/Mari_language" title="Mari language">Mari</a> <i>erge</i> 'son', <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> archaic <i>yrkä</i> 'young man'.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hungary" title="History of Hungary">History of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_895">Before 895</span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hungary&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2020</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_prehistory" title="Hungarian prehistory">Hungarian prehistory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_mythology" title="Hungarian mythology">Hungarian mythology</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg/220px-MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg/330px-MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg/440px-MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="999" data-file-height="680"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MorThanFeastofAttila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Attila, king of the Huns (434/444-453)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hungarian_warrior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hungarian_warrior.jpg/220px-Hungarian_warrior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hungarian_warrior.jpg/330px-Hungarian_warrior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hungarian_warrior.jpg/440px-Hungarian_warrior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="734" data-file-height="552"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hungarian_warrior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Italian fresco depicting a Hungarian warrior shooting backwards
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> conquered the territory west of the Danube River between 35 and 9&nbsp;BC. From 9&nbsp;BC to the end of the 4th century AD, <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>, the western part of the Carpathian Basin, was part of the Roman Empire. After the Western Roman Empire collapsed in the 5th century AD under the stress of the migration of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpi_(people)" title="Carpi (people)">Carpian</a> pressure, the Migration Period continued to bring many invaders into Central Europe, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Hunnic Empire</a> (c. 370–469). The most powerful ruler of the Hunnic Empire was <a href="/wiki/Attila_the_Hun" class="mw-redirect" title="Attila the Hun">Attila the Hun</a> (434–453), who later became a central figure in Hungarian mythology. After the disintegration of the Hunnic Empire, the <a href="/wiki/Gepids" title="Gepids">Gepids</a>, an Eastern Germanic tribe, who had been vassalized by the Huns, established their own kingdom in the Carpathian Basin. Other groups which reached the Carpathian Basin in the Migration Period were the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombards</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Slavs</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 560s, the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a> founded the Avar Khaganate, a state that maintained supremacy in the region for more than two centuries. The Franks under <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> defeated the Avars in a series of campaigns during the 790s. By the mid-9th century, the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Slavs#Principality" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian Slavs">Balaton Principality</a>, also known as Lower Pannonia, was established west of the Danube river as part of the Frankish <a href="/wiki/March_of_Pannonia" title="March of Pannonia">March of Pannonia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> conquered the lands east of the Danube river and took over the rule of the local Slavic tribes and remnants of the Avars. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Medieval_Hungary_.28895.E2.80.931526.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Hungary_(895–1526)">Medieval Hungary (895–1526)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Hungary" title="Principality of Hungary">Principality of Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_in_the_Middle_Ages" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Hungary in the Middle Ages">Kingdom of Hungary in the Middle Ages</a>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;">

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Munkacsy_Mihaly_Honfoglalas_(colored).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hungarian Conquest (of the Carpathian Basin) - painting by <a href="/wiki/Mih%C3%A1ly_Munk%C3%A1csy" title="Mihály Munkácsy">Mihály Munkácsy</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kalandozasok.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kalandozasok.jpg/220px-Kalandozasok.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kalandozasok.jpg/330px-Kalandozasok.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kalandozasok.jpg/440px-Kalandozasok.jpg 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="496"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kalandozasok.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_invasions_of_Europe" title="Hungarian invasions of Europe">Hungarian raids in the 10th century</a>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The freshly unified <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">Hungarians</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> led by <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d" title="Árpád">Árpád</a> (by tradition a descendant of Attila), settled in the Carpathian Basin starting in 895.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Country_Study:_Hungary_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Country_Study:_Hungary-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eliznik.org.uk_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eliznik.org.uk-44">[43]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_languages" title="Finno-Ugric languages">Finno-Ugrian theory</a>, they originated from an ancient <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic</a>-speaking population that formerly inhabited the forested area between the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a federation of united tribes, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Conquest_of_the_Carpathian_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Conquest of the Carpathian Basin">Hungary was established in 895</a>, some 50 years after the division of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a> in 843, before the unification of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Anglo-Saxon kingdoms</a>. Initially, the rising <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Hungary" title="Principality of Hungary">Principality of Hungary</a> ("Western Tourkia" in medieval Greek sources)<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> was a state created by a semi-nomadic people. It accomplished an enormous transformation into a Christian realm during the 10th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Stephen_Wyley_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen_Wyley-47">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This state was well-functioning, and the nation's military power allowed the Hungarians to conduct successful <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_invasions_of_Europe" title="Hungarian invasions of Europe">fierce campaigns and raids</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> to as far as today's Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-Stephen_Wyley_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen_Wyley-47">[46]</a></sup> The Hungarians defeated no fewer than <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_invasions_of_Europe" title="Hungarian invasions of Europe">three major East Frankish imperial armies</a> between 907 and 910.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> A later defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lechfeld" title="Battle of Lechfeld">Battle of Lechfeld</a> in 955 signaled a provisory end to most campaigns on foreign territories, at least towards the West. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Age_of_.C3.81rp.C3.A1dian_kings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_of_Árpádian_kings">Age of Árpádian kings</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d_dynasty" title="Árpád dynasty">Árpád dynasty</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/170px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/255px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/340px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="823" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>King <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">Saint Stephen</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/King_of_Hungary" title="King of Hungary">King of Hungary</a>, converted the nation to Christianity.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The year 972 marked the date when the ruling prince (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">fejedelem</i>) <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9za,_Grand_Prince_of_the_Hungarians" title="Géza, Grand Prince of the Hungarians">Géza</a> of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d_dynasty" title="Árpád dynasty">Árpád dynasty</a> officially started to integrate Hungary into Christian Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> His first-born son, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">Saint Stephen I</a>, became the first <a href="/wiki/King_of_Hungary" title="King of Hungary">King of Hungary</a> after defeating his <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> uncle <a href="/wiki/Kopp%C3%A1ny" title="Koppány">Koppány</a>, who also claimed the throne. Under Stephen, Hungary was recognised as a Catholic <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Apostolic Kingdom">Apostolic Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> Applying to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Sylvester_II" title="Pope Sylvester II">Pope Sylvester II</a>, Stephen received the insignia of royalty (including probably a part of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Crown_of_Hungary" title="Holy Crown of Hungary">Holy Crown of Hungary</a>, currently kept in the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Parliament_Building" title="Hungarian Parliament Building">Hungarian Parliament</a>) from the papacy. </p>
      <p>By 1006, Stephen consolidated his power, and started sweeping reforms to convert Hungary into a Western <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudal state</a>. The country switched to using the <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin language</a>, and until as late as 1844, Latin remained the official language of Hungary. Around this time, Hungary began to become a powerful kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ladislaus_I_of_Hungary" title="Ladislaus I of Hungary">Ladislaus I</a> extended Hungary's frontier in Transylvania and invaded <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Croatia_(medieval)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Croatia (medieval)">Croatia</a> in 1091.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> The Croatian campaign culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gvozd_Mountain" title="Battle of Gvozd Mountain">Battle of Gvozd Mountain</a> in 1097 and a <a href="/wiki/Croatia_in_personal_union_with_Hungary" title="Croatia in personal union with Hungary">personal union of Croatia and Hungary</a> in 1102, ruled by <a href="/wiki/Coloman_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Coloman of Hungary">Coloman</a> i.e. Könyves Kálmán.<sup id="cite_ref-HR-HU-Heka_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HR-HU-Heka-56">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg/170px-A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg/255px-A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg/340px-A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1750"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A_Szent_Korona_el%C3%B6lr%C5%91l_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Holy_Crown_of_Hungary" title="Holy Crown of Hungary">Holy Crown</a> (<i>Szent Korona</i>), one of the key symbols of Hungary
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg/220px-The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg/330px-The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg/440px-The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1119" data-file-height="1019"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Greek_Pantokrator_on_the_Hungarian_Holy_Crown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Jesus Christ, the Pantocrator on the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Crown_of_Hungary" title="Holy Crown of Hungary">Holy Crown of Hungary</a>. Hungary is traditionally a Christian country.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most powerful and wealthiest king of the Árpád dynasty was <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_III_of_Hungary" title="Béla III of Hungary">Béla III</a>, who disposed of the equivalent of 23 tonnes of pure silver a year. This exceeded the income of the French king (estimated at 17 tonnes) and was double the receipts of the English Crown.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Andrew_II_of_Hungary" title="Andrew II of Hungary">Andrew II</a> issued the <a href="/wiki/Diploma_Andreanum" title="Diploma Andreanum">Diploma Andreanum</a> which secured the special privileges of the <a href="/wiki/Transylvanian_Saxons" title="Transylvanian Saxons">Transylvanian Saxons</a> and is considered the first <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">Autonomy</a> law in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> He led the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Crusade" title="Fifth Crusade">Fifth Crusade</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> in 1217, setting up the largest royal army in the history of Crusades. His <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_1222" title="Golden Bull of 1222">Golden Bull of 1222</a> was the first constitution in <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>. The lesser nobles also began to present Andrew with grievances, a practice that evolved into the institution of the parliament (<i>parlamentum publicum</i>). </p>
      <p>In 1241–1242, the kingdom received a major blow with the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_invasion_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongolian invasion of Hungary">Mongol (Tatar) invasion</a>. Up to half of Hungary's then population of 2,000,000 were victims of the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> King Béla IV let <a href="/wiki/Cumans" title="Cumans">Cumans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jassic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Jassic people">Jassic people</a> into the country, who were fleeing the Mongols.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Over the centuries, they were fully assimilated into the Hungarian population.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a consequence, after the Mongols retreated, King Béla ordered the construction of hundreds of stone castles and fortifications, to defend against a possible second Mongol invasion. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Mongol_invasion_of_Hungary" title="Second Mongol invasion of Hungary">Mongols returned to Hungary</a> in 1285, but the newly built stone-castle systems and new tactics (using a higher proportion of heavily armed knights) stopped them. The invading Mongol force was defeated<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> near Pest by the royal army of Ladislaus IV of Hungary. As with later invasions, it was repelled handily, the Mongols losing much of their invading force. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_of_elected_kings">Age of elected kings</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Hungarian_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman–Hungarian Wars">Ottoman–Hungarian Wars</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png/320px-Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png/480px-Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png/640px-Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png 2x" data-file-width="1817" data-file-height="1120"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Louis%27s_kingdoms_and_his_vassal_territories.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of lands ruled by <a href="/wiki/Louis_I_of_Hungary" title="Louis I of Hungary">Louis the Great</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> reached one of its greatest extents during the Árpádian kings, yet royal power was weakened at the end of their rule in 1301. After a destructive period of <a href="/wiki/Interregnum" title="Interregnum">interregnum</a> (1301–1308), the first <a href="/wiki/Capetian_House_of_Anjou" title="Capetian House of Anjou">Angevin</a> king, <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Hungary" title="Charles I of Hungary">Charles I of Hungary</a> – a bilineal descendant of the Árpád dynasty – successfully restored royal power, and defeated oligarch rivals, the so-called "little kings". The second Angevin Hungarian king, <a href="/wiki/Louis_I_of_Hungary" title="Louis I of Hungary">Louis the Great</a> (1342–1382), led many successful military campaigns from Lithuania to Southern Italy (Kingdom of Naples), and was also <a href="/wiki/King_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Poland">King of Poland</a> from 1370. After King Louis died without a male heir, the country was stabilized only when <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund of Luxembourg</a> (1387–1437) succeeded to the throne, who in 1433 also became <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>. Sigismund was also (in several ways) a bilineal descendant of the Árpád dynasty. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_(1458-1490).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_%281458-1490%29.png/280px-The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_%281458-1490%29.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_%281458-1490%29.png/420px-The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_%281458-1490%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_%281458-1490%29.png/560px-The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_%281458-1490%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1700" data-file-height="1707"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_wars_of_Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary_(1458-1490).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Western conquests of <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus" title="Matthias Corvinus">Matthias Corvinus</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Bible_translation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bible translation">Bible translation</a> was completed in 1439. For half a year in 1437, there was an antifeudal and anticlerical peasant revolt in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Budai_Nagy_Antal_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Budai Nagy Antal Revolt">Budai Nagy Antal Revolt</a>, which was strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Hussite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussite">Hussite</a> ideas. </p>
      <p>From a small noble family in Transylvania, <a href="/wiki/John_Hunyadi" title="John Hunyadi">John Hunyadi</a> grew to become one of the country's most powerful lords, thanks to his outstanding capabilities as a mercenary commander. He was elected governor then regent. He was a successful crusader against the Ottoman Turks, one of his greatest victories being the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Belgrade_(1456)" title="Siege of Belgrade (1456)">Siege of Belgrade</a> in 1456. </p>
      <p>The last strong king of medieval Hungary was the Renaissance king <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus" title="Matthias Corvinus">Matthias Corvinus</a> (1458–1490), son of John Hunyadi. His election was the first time that a member of the nobility mounted to the Hungarian royal throne without dynastic background. He was a successful military leader and an enlightened patron of the arts and learning.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica1_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica1-63">[62]</a></sup> His library, the <a href="/wiki/Bibliotheca_Corviniana" title="Bibliotheca Corviniana">Bibliotheca Corviniana</a>, was Europe's greatest collection of historical chronicles, philosophic and scientific works in the 15th century, and second only in size to the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Library" title="Vatican Library">Vatican Library</a>. Items from the Bibliotheca Corviniana were inscribed on <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory of the World Register">Memory of the World Register</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The serfs and common people considered him a just ruler because he protected them from excessive demands and other abuses by the magnates.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> Under his rule, in 1479, the Hungarian army destroyed the Ottoman and Wallachian troops at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Breadfield" title="Battle of Breadfield">Battle of Breadfield</a>. Abroad he defeated the Polish and German imperial armies of Frederick at Breslau (<a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a>). Matthias' mercenary standing army, the <a href="/wiki/Black_Army_of_Hungary" title="Black Army of Hungary">Black Army of Hungary</a>, was an unusually large army for its time, and it conquered parts of Austria, Vienna (1485), and parts of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Decline_of_Hungary_.281490.E2.80.931526.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_of_Hungary_(1490–1526)">Decline of Hungary (1490–1526)</span></h4> 
      <p>King Matthias died without lawful sons, and the Hungarian magnates procured the accession of the Pole <a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Vladislaus II of Bohemia and Hungary">Vladislaus II</a> (1490–1516), supposedly because of his weak influence on Hungarian aristocracy.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica1_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica1-63">[62]</a></sup> Hungary's international role declined, its political stability shaken, and social progress was deadlocked.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> In 1514, the weakened old King Vladislaus II faced a major peasant rebellion led by <a href="/wiki/Gy%C3%B6rgy_D%C3%B3zsa" title="György Dózsa">György Dózsa</a>, which was ruthlessly crushed by the <a href="/wiki/Nobility_in_the_Kingdom_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobility in the Kingdom of Hungary">nobles</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/John_Z%C3%A1polya" title="John Zápolya">John Zápolya</a>. </p>
      <p>The resulting degradation of order paved the way for Ottoman pre-eminence. In 1521, the strongest Hungarian fortress in the South, Nándorfehérvár (today's <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, Serbia), <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Belgrade_(1521)" title="Siege of Belgrade (1521)">fell to the Turks</a>. The early appearance of Protestantism further worsened internal relations in the country. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Ottoman_wars_.281526.E2.80.931699.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_wars_(1526–1699)">Ottoman wars (1526–1699)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1526%E2%80%931867)" title="Kingdom of Hungary (1526–1867)">Kingdom of Hungary (1526–1867)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Hungary" title="Ottoman Hungary">Ottoman Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Transylvania_(1570%E2%80%931711)" title="Principality of Transylvania (1570–1711)">Principality of Transylvania (1570–1711)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Habsburg_wars" title="Ottoman–Habsburg wars">Ottoman–Habsburg wars</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9kely,_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Sz%C3%A9kely%2C_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-Sz%C3%A9kely%2C_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Sz%C3%A9kely%2C_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-Sz%C3%A9kely%2C_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Sz%C3%A9kely%2C_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-Sz%C3%A9kely%2C_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1884" data-file-height="2437"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9kely,_Bertalan_-_The_Women_of_Eger_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Painting commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Eger_(1552)" title="Siege of Eger (1552)">Siege of Eger</a>, a major victory against the Ottomans
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After some <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">150 years of wars</a> with the Hungarians and other states, the Ottomans gained a decisive victory over the Hungarian army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a> in 1526, where <a href="/wiki/Louis_II_of_Hungary" title="Louis II of Hungary">King Louis II</a> died while fleeing. Amid political chaos, the divided <a href="/wiki/Nobility_in_the_Kingdom_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobility in the Kingdom of Hungary">Hungarian nobility</a> elected two kings simultaneously, <a href="/wiki/John_Z%C3%A1polya" title="John Zápolya">John Zápolya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand I</a> of the Habsburg dynasty. With the conquest of Buda by the Turks in 1541, Hungary was divided into three parts and remained so until the end of the 17th century. The north-western part, termed as <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Hungary">Royal Hungary</a>, was annexed by the Habsburgs who ruled as Kings of Hungary. The eastern part of the kingdom became independent as the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Transylvania_(1571%E2%80%931711)" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Transylvania (1571–1711)">Principality of Transylvania</a>, under Ottoman (and later Habsburg) <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a>. The remaining central area, including the capital Buda, was known as the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Hungary" title="Ottoman Hungary">Pashalik of Buda</a>. </p>
      <p>The vast majority of the seventeen and nineteen thousand Ottoman soldiers in service in the Ottoman fortresses in the territory of Hungary were Orthodox and Muslim Balkan Slavs rather than ethnic Turkish people.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Orthodox Southern Slavs were also acting as <a href="/wiki/Akinji" title="Akinji">akinjis</a> and other light troops intended for pillaging in the territory of present-day Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In 1686, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1684)" title="Holy League (1684)">Holy League's</a> army, containing over 74,000 men from various nations, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buda_(1686)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Buda (1686)">reconquered Buda</a> from the Turks. After some more crushing <a href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_of_1716%E2%80%9318" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Turkish War of 1716–18">defeats of the Ottomans</a> in the next few years, the entire Kingdom of Hungary was removed from Ottoman rule by 1718. The last raid into Hungary by the Ottoman vassals <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Tatars</a> from <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> took place in 1717.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> The constrained Habsburg Counter-Reformation efforts in the 17th century reconverted the majority of the kingdom to Catholicism. The ethnic composition of Hungary was fundamentally changed as a consequence of the prolonged warfare with the Turks. A large part of the country became devastated, population growth was stunted, and many smaller settlements perished.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> The Austrian-Habsburg government settled large groups of Serbs and other Slavs in the depopulated south, and settled <a href="/wiki/Germans_of_Hungary" title="Germans of Hungary">Germans</a> (called <a href="/wiki/Danube_Swabians" title="Danube Swabians">Danube Swabians</a>) in various areas, but Hungarians were not allowed to settle or re-settle in the south of the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian Plain">Great Plain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="From_the_18th_century_to_World_War_I_.281699.E2.80.931918.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_18th_century_to_World_War_I_(1699–1918)">From the 18th century to World War I (1699–1918)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1848" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1848">Hungarian Revolution of 1848</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lands_of_the_Crown_of_Saint_Stephen" title="Lands of the Crown of Saint Stephen">Lands of the Crown of Saint Stephen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hungary_in_World_War_I" title="Hungary in World War I">Hungary in World War I</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%A1nyoki,_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/M%C3%A1nyoki%2C_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-M%C3%A1nyoki%2C_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/M%C3%A1nyoki%2C_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-M%C3%A1nyoki%2C_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/M%C3%A1nyoki%2C_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-M%C3%A1nyoki%2C_%C3%81dam_-_Portrait_of_Prince_Ferenc_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi_II_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2568" data-file-height="3124"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">

        <div class="thumbcaption">

         </div>Count <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_Sz%C3%A9chenyi" title="István Széchenyi">István Széchenyi</a> offered one year's income to establish the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Hungarian Academy of Sciences">Hungarian Academy of Sciences</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg/180px-E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg/270px-E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg/360px-E._Poulton_Portrait_of_Lajos_Kossuth_1860s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="445" data-file-height="577"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
