        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Austria-Hungary_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Austria-Hungary_map.svg/260px-Austria-Hungary_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Austria-Hungary_map.svg/390px-Austria-Hungary_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Austria-Hungary_map.svg/520px-Austria-Hungary_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="783" data-file-height="605"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Austria-Hungary_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Lands of the Crown of Saint Stephen</i> consisted of the territories of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> (16) and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Croatia-Slavonia" title="Kingdom of Croatia-Slavonia">Kingdom of Croatia-Slavonia</a> (17).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 1703 and 1711, there was a large-scale uprising led by <a href="/wiki/Francis_II_R%C3%A1k%C3%B3czi" title="Francis II Rákóczi">Francis II Rákóczi</a>, who after the dethronement of the Habsburgs in 1707 at the Diet of <a href="/wiki/%C3%93nod" title="Ónod">Ónod</a>, took power provisionally as the Ruling Prince of Hungary for the wartime period, but refused the Hungarian Crown and the title "King". The uprisings lasted for years. The Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Kuruc" title="Kuruc">Kuruc</a> army, although taking over most of the country, lost the main <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trencs%C3%A9n" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Trencsén">battle at Trencsén</a> (1708). Three years later, because of the growing desertion, defeatism and low morale, the Kuruc forces finally surrendered.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> and afterward, the Hungarian Diet had not convened for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> In the 1820s, the Emperor was forced to convene the Diet, which marked the beginning of a Reform Period (1825–1848, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">reformkor</i>). Count <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_Sz%C3%A9chenyi" title="István Széchenyi">István Széchenyi</a>, one of the most prominent statesmen of the country, recognised the urgent need for modernisation and his message got through. The Hungarian Parliament was reconvened in 1825 to handle financial needs. A liberal party emerged and focused on providing for the peasantry. <a href="/wiki/Lajos_Kossuth" title="Lajos Kossuth">Lajos Kossuth</a> – a famous journalist at that time – emerged as a leader of the lower <a href="/wiki/Gentry" title="Gentry">gentry</a> in the Parliament. A remarkable upswing started as the nation concentrated its forces on modernisation even though the Habsburg monarchs obstructed all important liberal laws relating to <a href="/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights" title="Civil and political rights">civil and political rights</a> and economic reforms. Many reformers (<a href="/wiki/Lajos_Kossuth" title="Lajos Kossuth">Lajos Kossuth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mih%C3%A1ly_T%C3%A1ncsics" title="Mihály Táncsics">Mihály Táncsics</a>) were imprisoned by the authorities. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg/260px-Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg/390px-Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg/520px-Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1540" data-file-height="1030"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Orsz%C3%A1ggy%C5%B1l%C3%A9s_megnyit%C3%A1sa_1848.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>5 July 1848: The opening ceremony of the first parliament, which was based on popular representation. The members of the first responsible government are on the balcony.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 15 March 1848, mass demonstrations in Pest and Buda enabled Hungarian reformists to push through a list of <a href="/wiki/12_points_of_the_Hungarian_Revolutionaries_of_1848" title="12 points of the Hungarian Revolutionaries of 1848">12 demands</a>. Under governor and president <a href="/wiki/Lajos_Kossuth" title="Lajos Kossuth">Lajos Kossuth</a> and the first Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Lajos_Batthy%C3%A1ny" title="Lajos Batthyány">Lajos Batthyány</a>, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> was dethroned. The Habsburg Ruler and his advisors skillfully manipulated the Croatian, Serbian and Romanian peasantry, led by priests and officers firmly loyal to the Habsburgs, and induced them to rebel against the Hungarian government, though the Hungarians were supported by the vast majority of the Slovak, German and <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">Rusyn</a> nationalities and by all the Jews of the kingdom, as well as by a large number of Polish, Austrian and Italian volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> In July 1849 the Hungarian Parliament proclaimed and enacted the first laws of ethnic and <a href="/wiki/Minority_rights" title="Minority rights">minority rights</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Many members of the nationalities gained the coveted highest positions within the Hungarian Army, like General <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Damjanich" title="János Damjanich">János Damjanich</a>, an ethnic Serb who became a Hungarian national hero through his command of the 3rd Hungarian Army Corps or <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Bem" title="Józef Bem">Józef Bem</a>, who was Polish and also became a national hero in Hungary. The Hungarian forces (<i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Hungarian_Landwehr" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Hungarian Landwehr">Honvédség</a></i>) defeated Austrian armies. To counter the successes of the Hungarian revolutionary army, Habsburg Emperor <a href="/wiki/Franz_Joseph_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Franz Joseph I">Franz Joseph I</a> asked for help from the "Gendarme of Europe", Tsar <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">Nicholas I</a>, whose Russian armies invaded Hungary. This made <a href="/wiki/Art%C3%BAr_G%C3%B6rgey" class="mw-redirect" title="Artúr Görgey">Artúr Görgey</a> surrender in August 1849. The leader of the Austrian army, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Jacob_von_Haynau" title="Julius Jacob von Haynau">Julius Jacob von Haynau</a>, became governor of Hungary for a few months and ordered the execution of <a href="/wiki/The_13_Martyrs_of_Arad" title="The 13 Martyrs of Arad">the 13 Martyrs of Arad</a>, leaders of the Hungarian army, and Prime Minister Batthyány in October 1849. Lajos Kossuth escaped into exile. Following the war of 1848&nbsp;– 1849, the whole country was in "passive resistance". </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg/260px-Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg/390px-Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg/520px-Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="894" data-file-height="577"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ferenc_J%C3%B3zsef_koron%C3%A1z%C3%A1sa_Bud%C3%A1n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_Hungarian_monarch" title="Coronation of the Hungarian monarch">Coronation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Franz_Joseph_I_of_Austria" title="Franz Joseph I of Austria">Francis Joseph I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empress_Elisabeth_of_Austria" title="Empress Elisabeth of Austria">Elisabeth Amalie</a> at <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Church" title="Matthias Church">Matthias Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buda" title="Buda">Buda</a>, 8 June 1867.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Because of external and internal problems, reforms seemed inevitable, and major military defeats of Austria forced the Habsburgs to negotiate the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Compromise_of_1867" title="Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867">Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867</a>, by which the dual Monarchy of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> was formed. This Empire had the second largest area in Europe (after the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>), and it was the third most populous (after Russia and the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>). The two realms were governed separately by two parliaments from two capital cities, with a common monarch and common external and military policies. Economically, the empire was a customs union. The old Hungarian Constitution was restored, and Franz Joseph I was crowned as <a href="/wiki/King_of_Hungary" title="King of Hungary">King of Hungary</a>. The era witnessed impressive economic development. The formerly backward Hungarian economy became relatively modern and industrialised by the turn of the 20th century, although agriculture remained dominant until 1890. In 1873, the old capital <a href="/wiki/Buda" title="Buda">Buda</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%93buda" title="Óbuda">Óbuda</a> were officially united with <a href="/wiki/Pest,_Hungary" title="Pest, Hungary">Pest</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> thus creating the new metropolis of <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>. Many of the state institutions and the modern administrative system of Hungary were established during this period. </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand" title="Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand">Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand</a> in Sarajevo, the Hungarian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_Tisza" title="István Tisza">István Tisza</a> and his cabinet tried to avoid the outbreak and escalating of a war in Europe, but their diplomatic efforts were unsuccessful. <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> drafted 9&nbsp;million (fighting forces: 7.8&nbsp;million) soldiers in World War I (over 4&nbsp;million from the Kingdom of Hungary) on the side of Germany, Bulgaria, and Turkey. The troops raised in the Kingdom of Hungary spent little time defending the actual territory of Hungary, with the exceptions of the <a href="/wiki/Brusilov_Offensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Brusilov Offensive">Brusilov Offensive</a> in June 1916, and a few months later, when the Romanian army made an attack into Transylvania,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Self-published_sources" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on a self-published source. (January 2021)">self-published source?</span></a></i>]</sup> both of which were repelled. In comparison, of the total army, Hungary's loss ratio was more than any other nation of Austria-Hungary. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> conquered Serbia. Romania declared war. The Central Powers conquered Southern Romania and the Romanian capital <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>. In 1916 Emperor Franz Joseph died, and the new monarch <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles IV of Hungary">Charles IV</a> sympathized with the pacifists. With great difficulty, the Central powers stopped and repelled the attacks of the Russian Empire. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Szent_Istvan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Szent_Istvan.jpg/220px-Szent_Istvan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Szent_Istvan.jpg/330px-Szent_Istvan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Szent_Istvan.jpg/440px-Szent_Istvan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="861" data-file-height="460"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Szent_Istvan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hungarian-built <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnought</a> battleship <a href="/wiki/SMS_Szent_Istv%C3%A1n" title="SMS Szent István">SMS <i>Szent István</i></a> in World War I
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Eastern front of the Allied (<a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Entente</a>) Powers completely collapsed. The Austro-Hungarian Empire then withdrew from all defeated countries. On the Italian front, the Austro-Hungarian army made no progress against Italy after January 1918. Despite great Eastern successes, Germany suffered complete defeat on the more important Western front. By 1918, the economic situation had deteriorated (strikes in factories were organised by leftist and pacifist movements) and uprisings in the army had become commonplace. In the capital cities, the Austrian and Hungarian leftist liberal movements (the maverick parties) and their leaders supported the separatism of ethnic minorities. Austria-Hungary signed a general armistice in <a href="/wiki/Padua" title="Padua">Padua</a> on 3 November 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> In October 1918, Hungary's union with Austria was dissolved. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Between_the_World_Wars_.281918.E2.80.931941.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_the_World_Wars_(1918–1941)">Between the World Wars (1918–1941)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungary_between_the_World_Wars" title="Hungary between the World Wars">Hungary between the World Wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_interwar_economy" title="Hungarian interwar economy">Hungarian interwar economy</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Trianon_consequences.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Trianon_consequences.png/220px-Trianon_consequences.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Trianon_consequences.png/330px-Trianon_consequences.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Trianon_consequences.png/440px-Trianon_consequences.png 2x" data-file-width="1140" data-file-height="774"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Trianon_consequences.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>With the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a>, Hungary lost 72% of its territory, its sea ports and 3,425,000 ethnic Hungarians<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup>
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#cd3318; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Majority Hungarian areas (according to the 1910 census) detached from Hungary
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the First World War, Hungary underwent a period of profound political upheaval, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Aster_Revolution" title="Aster Revolution">Aster Revolution</a> in 1918, which brought the social-democratic <a href="/wiki/Mih%C3%A1ly_K%C3%A1rolyi" title="Mihály Károlyi">Mihály Károlyi</a> to power as Prime Minister. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hungarian_Honv%C3%A9d" title="Royal Hungarian Honvéd">Hungarian Royal Honvéd army</a> still had more than 1,400,000 soldiers<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> when Mihály Károlyi was announced as prime minister of Hungary. Károlyi yielded to U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>'s demand for <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">pacifism</a> by ordering the disarmament of the Hungarian army. This happened under the direction of <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Linder" title="Béla Linder">Béla Linder</a>, minister of war in the Károlyi government.<sup id="cite_ref-Dixon_1986_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dixon_1986-83">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sharp_2008_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharp_2008-84">[83]</a></sup> Due to the full disarmament of its army, Hungary was to remain without a national defence at a time of particular vulnerability. During the rule of Károlyi's pacifist cabinet, Hungary lost control over approx. 75% of its former pre-WW1 territories (325 411&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) without a fight and was subject to foreign occupation. The <a href="/wiki/Little_Entente" title="Little Entente">Little Entente</a>, sensing an opportunity, invaded the country from three sides—Romania <a href="/wiki/Hungarian-Romanian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian-Romanian War">invaded</a> <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, Czechoslovakia annexed <a href="/wiki/Upper_Hungary" title="Upper Hungary">Upper Hungary</a> (today's Slovakia), and a joint <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serb</a>-<a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French</a> coalition annexed <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> and other southern regions. In March 1919, communists led by <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Kun" title="Béla Kun">Béla Kun</a> ousted the Károlyi government and proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Hungarian Soviet Republic">Hungarian Soviet Republic</a> (<i>Tanácsköztársaság</i>), followed by a thorough <a href="/wiki/Red_Terror_(Hungary)" title="Red Terror (Hungary)">Red Terror</a> campaign. Despite some successes on the Czechoslovak front, Kun's forces were ultimately unable to resist the Romanian invasion; by August 1919, Romanian troops occupied Budapest and ousted Kun. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg/170px-Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg/255px-Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg/340px-Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1416" data-file-height="1904"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portraits_de_Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy" title="Miklós Horthy">Miklós Horthy</a>, Regent of the Kingdom of Hungary (1920–1944)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In November 1919, rightist forces led by former Austro-Hungarian admiral <a href="/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy" title="Miklós Horthy">Miklós Horthy</a> entered Budapest; exhausted by the war and its aftermath, the populace accepted Horthy's leadership. In January 1920, parliamentary elections were held and Horthy was proclaimed Regent of the reestablished <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1920%E2%80%9346)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Hungary (1920–46)">Kingdom of Hungary</a>, inaugurating the so-called "Horthy era" (<i>Horthy-kor</i>). The new government worked quickly to normalize foreign relations while turning a blind eye to a <a href="/wiki/White_Terror_(Hungary)" title="White Terror (Hungary)">White Terror</a> that swept through the countryside; extrajudicial killings of suspected communists and Jews lasted well into 1920. On 4 June of that year, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a> established new borders for Hungary. The country lost 71% of its territory and 66% of its antebellum population, as well as many sources of raw materials and its sole <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rijeka" title="Rijeka">Fiume</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Macartney37_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macartney37-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> Though the revision of the Treaty quickly rose to the top of the national political agenda, the Horthy government was not willing to resort to military intervention to do so. </p>
      <p>The initial years of the Horthy regime were preoccupied with putsch attempts by <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles IV of Hungary">Charles IV</a>, the Austro-Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Pretender" title="Pretender">pretender</a>; continued suppression of communists; and a migration crisis triggered by the Trianon territorial changes. Though free elections continued, Horthy's personality, and those of his personally selected prime ministers, dominated the political scene. The government's actions continued to drift right with the passage of antisemitic laws and, due to the continued isolation of the Little Entente, economic and then political gravitation towards <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy#Fascist_regime_(1922–1943)" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> further exacerbated the situation and the popularity of fascist politicians such as <a href="/wiki/Gyula_G%C3%B6mb%C3%B6s" title="Gyula Gömbös">Gyula Gömbös</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Sz%C3%A1lasi" title="Ferenc Szálasi">Ferenc Szálasi</a>, promising economic and social recovery, rose. </p>
      <p>Horthy's nationalist agenda reached its apogee in 1938 and 1940, when the Nazis rewarded Hungary's staunchly pro-Germany foreign policy in the <a href="/wiki/First_Vienna_Award" title="First Vienna Award">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Vienna_Award" title="Second Vienna Award">Second Vienna Awards</a>, respectively, peacefully restoring ethnic-Hungarian-majority areas lost after Trianon. In 1939, Hungary regained further territory from Czechoslovakia <a href="/wiki/Slovak-Hungarian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak-Hungarian War">through force</a>. Hungary <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">formally joined</a> the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a> on 20 November 1940, and in 1941, participated in the <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="German invasion of Yugoslavia">invasion of Yugoslavia</a>, gaining some of its former territories in the south. </p> 
      <h3><span id="World_War_II_.281941.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_(1941–1945)">World War II (1941–1945)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungary_during_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungary during World War II">Hungary during World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust in Hungary">Holocaust in Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet occupation of Hungary">Soviet occupation of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png/310px-Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png/465px-Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png/620px-Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2157"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hungary_1941-44_Administrative_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kingdom of Hungary, 1941–44
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary formally entered World War II as an Axis Power on 26 June 1941, declaring war on the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> after unidentified planes bombed <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">Kassa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munkacheve" class="mw-redirect" title="Munkacheve">Munkács</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rakhiv" title="Rakhiv">Rahó</a>. Hungarian troops fought on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a> for two years. Despite <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Uman" title="Battle of Uman">some early successes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130-87">[86]</a></sup> the Hungarian government began seeking a secret peace pact with <a href="/wiki/Allies_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Allies (World War II)">the Allies</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Second_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Second Army">Second Army</a> suffered catastrophic losses <a href="/wiki/Ostrogozhsk%E2%80%93Rossosh_Offensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostrogozhsk–Rossosh Offensive">at the River Don</a> in January 1943. Learning of the planned defection, German troops <a href="/wiki/Operation_Margarethe" title="Operation Margarethe">occupied Hungary</a> on 19 March 1944 to guarantee Horthy's compliance. In October, as the Soviet front approached and the Hungarian government made further efforts to disengage from the war, German troops ousted Horthy and installed a puppet government under Szálasi's fascist <a href="/wiki/Arrow_Cross_Party" title="Arrow Cross Party">Arrow Cross Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130-87">[86]</a></sup> Szálasi pledged all the country's capabilities in service of the German war machine. By October 1944, the Soviets had reached the river Tisza, and despite <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Debrecen" title="Battle of Debrecen">some losses</a>, succeeded in encircling and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Budapest" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Budapest">besieging Budapest</a> in December. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08,_Budapest,_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08%2C_Budapest%2C_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08%2C_Budapest%2C_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08%2C_Budapest%2C_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08%2C_Budapest%2C_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08%2C_Budapest%2C_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08%2C_Budapest%2C_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="796" data-file-height="512"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-680-8285A-08,_Budapest,_Festnahme_von_Juden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> women being arrested on Wesselényi Street in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> during <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 20–22 October 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After German occupation, Hungary <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust in Hungary">participated</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-no-warning-to-hungary-jews_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-no-warning-to-hungary-jews-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> During the German occupation in May–June 1944, the Arrow Cross and Hungarian police deported nearly 440,000 Jews, mainly to <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a>. Nearly all of them were murdered.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> The Swedish Diplomat <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Wallenberg" title="Raoul Wallenberg">Raoul Wallenberg</a> managed to save a considerable number of Hungarian Jews by giving them Swedish passports.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rezs%C5%91_Kasztner" title="Rezső Kasztner">Rezső Kasztner</a>, one of the leaders of the Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Aid_and_Rescue_Committee" title="Aid and Rescue Committee">Aid and Rescue Committee</a>, bribed senior SS officers such as <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">Adolf Eichmann</a> to allow some Jews to escape.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> The Horthy government's complicity in the Holocaust remains a point of controversy and contention. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg/220px-Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg/330px-Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg/440px-Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2748"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lanc_hid_-_Budapest_3_Febr_1946_Foto_Takkk_Hungary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge" title="Széchenyi Chain Bridge">Széchenyi Chain Bridge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Buda_Castle" title="Buda Castle">Buda Castle</a> in ruins after World War II (1946)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The war left Hungary devastated, destroying over 60% of the economy and causing significant <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties#endnote_Hungary" title="World War II casualties">loss of life</a>. In addition to the over 600,000 Hungarian Jews killed,<sup id="cite_ref-ind09/96_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind09/96-96">[95]</a></sup> as many as 280,000<sup id="cite_ref-EU38_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU38-97">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> other Hungarians were raped, murdered and executed or deported for slave labour by Czechoslovaks,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Soviet <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> troops,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> and Yugoslavs.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 February 1945, Budapest surrendered; by April, German troops left the country under Soviet military occupation. 200,000 Hungarians were expelled from Czechoslovakia in exchange for 70,000 Slovaks living in Hungary. 202,000 ethnic Germans were expelled to Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> and through the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Treaties" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Peace Treaties">Paris Peace Treaties</a>, Hungary was again reduced to its immediate post-Trianon borders. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Communism_.281945.E2.80.931989.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Communism_(1945–1989)">Communism (1945–1989)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Republic_(1946%E2%80%9349)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Republic (1946–49)">Hungarian Republic (1946–49)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic" title="Hungarian People's Republic">Hungarian People's Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">Hungarian Revolution of 1956</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the defeat of Nazi Germany, Hungary became a <a href="/wiki/Soviet_satellite" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet satellite">satellite state</a> of the Soviet Union. The Soviet leadership selected <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ty%C3%A1s_R%C3%A1kosi" title="Mátyás Rákosi">Mátyás Rákosi</a> to front the <a href="/wiki/Stalinization" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalinization">Stalinization</a> of the country, and Rákosi <i>de facto</i> ruled Hungary from 1949 to 1956. His government's policies of militarization, industrialisation, collectivization, and war compensation led to a severe decline in living standards. In imitation of Stalin's <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a>, the Rákosi government established a secret political police, the <a href="/wiki/State_Protection_Authority" title="State Protection Authority">ÁVH</a>, to enforce the new regime. In the ensuing purges, approximately 350,000 officials and intellectuals were imprisoned or executed from 1948 to 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Many freethinkers, democrats, and Horthy-era dignitaries were secretly arrested and extrajudicially interned in domestic and foreign <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Gulags</a>. Some 600,000 Hungarians were deported to Soviet labour camps, where at least 200,000 died.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/220px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/330px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/440px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2243" data-file-height="1552"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A destroyed Soviet tank in Budapest during the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">1956 Revolution</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Time_Magazine_Person_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Magazine Person of the Year">Man of the Year</a> for 1956 was the Hungarian Freedom Fighter<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Stalin's death in 1953, the Soviet Union pursued a programme of <a href="/wiki/Destalinization" class="mw-redirect" title="Destalinization">destalinization</a> that was inimical to Rákosi, leading to his deposition. The following political cooling saw the ascent of <a href="/wiki/Imre_Nagy" title="Imre Nagy">Imre Nagy</a> to the premiership and the growing interest of students and intellectuals in political life. Nagy promised market liberalization and political openness, while Rákosi opposed both vigorously. Rákosi eventually managed to discredit Nagy and replace him with the more hard-line <a href="/wiki/Ern%C5%91_Ger%C5%91" title="Ernő Gerő">Ernő Gerő</a>. Hungary joined the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> in May 1955, as societal dissatisfaction with the regime swelled. Following the firing on peaceful demonstrations by Soviet soldiers and secret police, and rallies throughout the country on 23 October 1956, protesters took to the streets in Budapest, initiating the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">1956 Revolution</a>. In an effort to quell the chaos, Nagy returned as premier, promised free elections, and took Hungary out of the Warsaw Pact. </p>
      <p>The violence nonetheless continued as revolutionary militias sprung up against the Soviet Army and the ÁVH; the roughly 3,000-strong resistance fought Soviet tanks using <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">Molotov cocktails</a> and machine-pistols. Though the preponderance of the Soviets was immense, they suffered heavy losses, and by 30 October 1956, most Soviet troops had withdrawn from Budapest to garrison the countryside. For a time, the Soviet leadership was unsure how to respond to developments in Hungary but eventually decided to intervene to prevent a destabilization of the Soviet bloc. On 4 November, reinforcements of more than 150,000 troops and 2,500 tanks entered the country from the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> Nearly 20,000 Hungarians were killed resisting the intervention, while an additional 21,600 were imprisoned afterward for political reasons. Some 13,000 were interned and 230 brought to trial and executed. Nagy was secretly tried, found guilty, sentenced to death, and executed by hanging in June 1958. Because borders were briefly opened, nearly a quarter of a million people fled the country by the time the revolution was suppressed.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="K.C3.A1d.C3.A1r_era_.281956.E2.80.931988.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kádár_era_(1956–1988)">Kádár era (1956–1988)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Goulash_Communism" title="Goulash Communism">Goulash Communism</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg/170px-J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg/255px-J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg/340px-J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1380" data-file-height="1908"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r_1962.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r" title="János Kádár">János Kádár</a>, General Secretary of MSZMP, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Hungarian Socialist Workers' Party">Hungarian Socialist Workers' Party</a> (1956–1988)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After a second, briefer period of Soviet military occupation, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_K%C3%A1d%C3%A1r" title="János Kádár">János Kádár</a>, Nagy's former Minister of State, was chosen by the Soviet leadership to head the new government and chair the new ruling <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Hungarian Socialist Workers' Party">Socialist Workers' Party</a> (MSzMP). Kádár quickly normalized the situation. In 1963, the government granted a general amnesty and released the majority of those imprisoned for their active participation in the uprising. Kádár proclaimed a new policy line, according to which the people were no longer compelled to profess loyalty to the party if they tacitly accepted the Socialist regime as a fact of life. In many speeches, he described this as, "Those who are not against us are with us." Kádár introduced new planning priorities in the economy, such as allowing farmers significant plots of private land within the collective farm system (<i>háztáji gazdálkodás</i>). The living standard rose as consumer goods and food production took precedence over military production, which was reduced to one-tenth of pre-revolutionary levels. </p>
      <p>In 1968, the <a href="/wiki/New_Economic_Mechanism" title="New Economic Mechanism">New Economic Mechanism</a> (NEM) introduced free-market elements into the socialist command economy. From the 1960s through the late 1980s, Hungary was often referred to as "<a href="/wiki/The_happiest_barrack" class="mw-redirect" title="The happiest barrack">the happiest barrack</a>" within the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern bloc">Eastern bloc</a>. During the latter part of the Cold War Hungary's <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> was fourth only to <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic">Czechoslovakia</a>, and the Soviet Union itself.<sup id="cite_ref-madison185_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-madison185-115">[114]</a></sup> As a result of this relatively high standard of living, a more liberalized economy, a less censored press, and less restricted travel rights, Hungary was generally considered one of the more liberal countries in which to live in Central Europe during communism. In the 1980s, however, living standards steeply declined again due to <a href="/wiki/Early_1980s_recession" title="Early 1980s recession">a worldwide recession</a> to which communism was unable to respond.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> By the time Kádár died in 1989, the Soviet Union was in steep decline and a younger generation of reformists saw liberalization as the solution to economic and social issues. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Third_Republic_.281989.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_Republic_(1989–present)">Third Republic (1989–present)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">Revolutions of 1989</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_protests_in_Hungary" title="2006 protests in Hungary">2006 protests in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Foundation_of_the_Visegr%C3%A1d_Group.tiff" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> signing ceremony in February 1991
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary's <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_communism" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of communism">transition from communism</a> to democracy and capitalism (<i>rendszerváltás</i>, "regime change") was peaceful and prompted by economic stagnation, domestic political pressure, and changing relations with other <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> countries. Although the MSzMP began <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Round_Table_Talks" title="Hungarian Round Table Talks">Round Table Talks</a> with various opposition groups in March 1989, the reburial of Imre Nagy as a revolutionary martyr that June is widely considered the symbolic end of communism in Hungary. Over 100,000 people attended the Budapest ceremony without any significant government interference, and many speakers openly called for Soviet troops to leave the country. Free elections were held <a href="/wiki/1990_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="1990 Hungarian parliamentary election">in May 1990</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Democratic_Forum" title="Hungarian Democratic Forum">Hungarian Democratic Forum</a>, a major conservative opposition group, was elected to the head of a coalition government. <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zsef_Antall" title="József Antall">József Antall</a> became the first democratically elected Prime Minister since World War II. </p>
      <p>With the removal of state subsidies and rapid privatization in 1991, Hungary was affected by a severe economic recession. The Antall government's austerity measures proved unpopular, and the Communist Party's legal and political heir, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Socialist_Party" title="Hungarian Socialist Party">Socialist Party</a>, won the subsequent <a href="/wiki/1994_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="1994 Hungarian parliamentary election">1994 elections</a>. This abrupt shift in the political landscape was repeated in <a href="/wiki/1998_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="1998 Hungarian parliamentary election">1998</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="2002 Hungarian parliamentary election">2002</a>; each electoral cycle, the governing party was ousted and the erstwhile opposition elected. Like most other post-communist European states, however, Hungary broadly pursued an <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">integrationist</a> agenda, <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">joining</a> <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 1999 and the European Union <a href="/wiki/2003_Hungarian_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2003 Hungarian European Union membership referendum">in 2004</a>. As a NATO member, Hungary was involved in the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/2006_protests_in_Hungary" title="2006 protests in Hungary">major protests</a> erupted after it was revealed that Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Gyurcs%C3%A1ny" title="Ferenc Gyurcsány">Ferenc Gyurcsány</a> had claimed in <a href="/wiki/%C5%90sz%C3%B6d_speech" title="Őszöd speech">a private speech</a> that <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Socialist_Party" title="Hungarian Socialist Party">his party</a> "lied" to win the <a href="/wiki/2006_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="2006 Hungarian parliamentary election">recent elections</a>. The popularity of left-wing parties plummeted in the ensuing political upheaval, and in 2010, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orbán">Viktor Orbán</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_conservatism" title="National conservatism">national-conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Fidesz" title="Fidesz">Fidesz</a> was <a href="/wiki/2010_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="2010 Hungarian parliamentary election">elected</a> to a parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">supermajority</a>. The legislature consequently approved a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Hungary" title="Constitution of Hungary">new constitution</a>, among other sweeping governmental and legal changes. Although these developments were met with and still engender controversy, Fidesz secured a second parliamentary supermajority <a href="/wiki/2014_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="2014 Hungarian parliamentary election">in 2014</a> and a third <a href="/wiki/2018_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="2018 Hungarian parliamentary election">in 2018</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2018, the European parliament voted to act against Hungary, under the terms of <a href="/wiki/Article_7_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Article 7 of the Treaty on European Union">Article 7 of the Treaty on European Union</a>. Proponents of the vote claimed that the Hungarian government posed a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_backsliding" title="Democratic backsliding">"systematic threat" to democracy</a> and the rule of law. The vote was carried with the support of 448 MEPs, narrowly clearing the two-thirds majority required. The vote marked the first the European parliament had triggered an article 7 procedure against an EU member state. <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9ter_Szijj%C3%A1rt%C3%B3" title="Péter Szijjártó">Péter Szijjártó</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Hungary)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (Hungary)">Hungarian foreign minister</a>, described the vote as "petty revenge" which had been provoked by Hungary's tough anti-migration policies. Szijjártó alleged that the vote was fraudulent because abstentions were not counted which made it easier to reach the two-thirds majority required to pass the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the <a href="/wiki/European_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="European elections">European elections</a> in May 2019, Viktor Orbán's Fidesz Party secured another a sweeping victory, receiving more than 50% of the votes.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> In October 2019, the opposition won mayoral election in capital Budapest, meaning prime minister Orbán and the <a href="/wiki/Fidesz-KDNP" class="mw-redirect" title="Fidesz-KDNP">Fidesz-KDNP</a> governing coalition got first major electoral blow since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2020, during the ongoing <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Hungary" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Hungary">coronavirus pandemic</a>, the Hungarian parliament passed a law granting the Government the power to rule by decree to the extent it is necessary to diminish the consequences of the pandemic, suspending <a href="/wiki/By-elections" class="mw-redirect" title="By-elections">by-elections</a> and outlawing the "spreading of misinformation"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The new law actually modified the definition of fearmongering. (April 2020)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The Government's special authorisation is in force until the pandemic is declared to have ended.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The law granting the Government the power to rule by decree was lifted on 16 June 2020, as the emergency situation concerning the pandemic had ended.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Hungary" title="Geography of Hungary">Geography of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Hungary" title="List of national parks of Hungary">List of national parks of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Magyar_racka_juh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Magyar_racka_juh.jpg/220px-Magyar_racka_juh.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Magyar_racka_juh.jpg/330px-Magyar_racka_juh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Magyar_racka_juh.jpg/440px-Magyar_racka_juh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Magyar_racka_juh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A flock of <a href="/wiki/Racka" title="Racka">Racka</a> sheep in the <a href="/wiki/Fert%C5%91-Hans%C3%A1g_National_Park" title="Fertő-Hanság National Park">Fertő-Hanság National Park</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary's geography has traditionally been defined by its two main waterways, the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tisza" title="Tisza">Tisza</a> rivers. The common tripartite division of the country into three sections—<i>Dunántúl</i> ("beyond the Danube", <a href="/wiki/Transdanubia" title="Transdanubia">Transdanubia</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Tisz%C3%A1nt%C3%BAl" title="Tiszántúl">Tiszántúl</a></i> ("beyond the Tisza"), and <i>Duna-Tisza köze</i> ("between the Danube and Tisza")—is a reflection of this. The Danube flows north–south right through the centre of contemporary Hungary, and the entire country lies within its <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basin</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Transdanubia" title="Transdanubia">Transdanubia</a>, which stretches westward from the centre of the country towards Austria, is a primarily hilly region with a terrain varied by low mountains. These include the very eastern stretch of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alpokalja" title="Alpokalja">Alpokalja</a></i>, in the west of the country, the <a href="/wiki/Transdanubian_Mountains" title="Transdanubian Mountains">Transdanubian Mountains</a> in the central region of Transdanubia, and the <a href="/wiki/Mecsek" title="Mecsek">Mecsek</a> Mountains and <a href="/wiki/Vill%C3%A1ny_Mountains" title="Villány Mountains">Villány Mountains</a> in the south. The highest point of the area is the Írott-kő in the Alps, at 882 metres (2,894&nbsp;ft). The <a href="/wiki/Little_Hungarian_Plain" title="Little Hungarian Plain">Little Hungarian Plain</a> (<i>Kisalföld</i>) is found in northern Transdanubia. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Balaton" title="Lake Balaton">Lake Balaton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_H%C3%A9v%C3%ADz" title="Lake Hévíz">Lake Hévíz</a>, the largest lake in Central Europe and the largest thermal lake in the world, respectively, are in Transdanubia as well. </p>
      <p>The <i>Duna-Tisza köze</i> and <i>Tiszántúl</i> are characterised mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Hungarian_Plain" title="Great Hungarian Plain">Great Hungarian Plain</a> (<i>Alföld</i>), which stretches across most of the eastern and southeastern areas of the country. To the north of the Plain are the foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a> in a wide band near the <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakian</a> border. The <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9kes" title="Kékes">Kékes</a> at 1,014&nbsp;m or 3,327&nbsp;ft is the tallest mountain in Hungary and is found here. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Hungary belongs to the Central European province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, the territory of Hungary belongs to the terrestrial ecoregion of <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_mixed_forests" title="Pannonian mixed forests">Pannonian mixed forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-131">[130]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 2.25/10, ranking it 156th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-132">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Hungary has 10 national parks, 145 minor nature reserves, and 35 landscape protection areas. </p>
      <p>Hungary is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <p>Hungary has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate seasonal climate</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> with generally warm summers with low overall humidity levels but frequent rainshowers and cold snowy winters. Average annual temperature is 9.7&nbsp;°C (49.5&nbsp;°F). Temperature extremes are 41.9&nbsp;°C (107.4&nbsp;°F) on 20 July 2007 at Kiskunhalas in the summer and −35&nbsp;°C (−31.0&nbsp;°F) on 16 February 1940 Miskolc-Görömbölytapolca in the winter. Average high temperature in the summer is 23 to 28&nbsp;°C (73 to 82&nbsp;°F) and average low temperature in the winter is −3 to −7&nbsp;°C (27 to 19&nbsp;°F). The average yearly rainfall is approximately 600&nbsp;mm (23.6&nbsp;in). </p>
      <p>Hungary is ranked sixth in an environmental protection index by <i>GW</i>/<i><a href="/wiki/Climate_Action_Network" title="Climate Action Network">CAN</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Hungary" title="Politics of Hungary">Politics of Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Hungary" title="Government of Hungary">Government of Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Hungary" title="Taxation in Hungary">Taxation in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:281px;max-width:281px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ader_Janos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Ader_Janos.jpg/130px-Ader_Janos.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="198" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Ader_Janos.jpg/195px-Ader_Janos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Ader_Janos.jpg/260px-Ader_Janos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2316" data-file-height="3519"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_%C3%81der" title="János Áder">János Áder</a>,
           <br><small><a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Hungary" title="List of heads of state of Hungary">President</a> since 2012</small>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:145px;max-width:145px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg/143px-Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg" decoding="async" width="143" height="198" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg/215px-Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg/286px-Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n_Tallinn_Digital_Summit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1092" data-file-height="1511"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orbán">Viktor Orbán</a>,
           <br><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Hungary" title="Prime Minister of Hungary">Prime Minister</a> since 2010</small>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democratic">parliamentary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">republic</a>. The Hungarian political system operates under a framework reformed in 2012; this constitutional document is the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Hungary" title="Constitution of Hungary">Fundamental Law of Hungary</a>. Amendments generally require a two-thirds majority of parliament; the fundamental principles of the constitution (as expressed in the articles guaranteeing human dignity, the separation of powers, the state structure, and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>) are valid in perpetuity. 199 Members of Parliament (<i>országgyűlési képviselő</i>) are elected to the highest organ of state authority, the <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <i><a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Hungary">Országgyűlés</a></i> (National Assembly), every four years in a single-round <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a> election with an <a href="/wiki/Election_threshold" class="mw-redirect" title="Election threshold">election threshold</a> of 5%. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg/220px-S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg/330px-S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg/440px-S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4448" data-file-height="2945"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A1ndor-palota_naps%C3%BCt%C3%A9sben.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1ndor_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Sándor Palace">Sándor Palace</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residence</a> of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Hungary" title="President of Hungary">President of Hungary</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_(31363963556).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_%2831363963556%29.jpg/220px-Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_%2831363963556%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_%2831363963556%29.jpg/330px-Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_%2831363963556%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_%2831363963556%29.jpg/440px-Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_%2831363963556%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3825" data-file-height="2295"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Budapest_Hungarian_Parliament_(31363963556).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Parliament_Building" title="Hungarian Parliament Building">Hungarian Parliament Building</a> on the bank of the Danube in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Hungary" title="President of Hungary">President of the Republic</a> (<i>köztársasági elnök</i>) serves as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and is elected by the National Assembly every five years. The president is invested primarily with representative responsibilities and powers: receiving foreign heads of state, formally nominating the Prime Minister at the recommendation of the National Assembly, and serving as <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Army">armed forces</a>. Importantly, the president is also invested with <a href="/wiki/Veto_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Veto power">veto power</a> and may send legislation to the 15-member <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Hungary" title="Constitutional Court of Hungary">Constitutional Court</a> for review. The third most significant governmental position in Hungary is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_National_Assembly_(Hungary)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Speakers of the National Assembly (Hungary)">Speaker of the National Assembly</a>, who is elected by the National Assembly and responsible for overseeing the daily sessions of the body. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Hungary" title="Prime Minister of Hungary">Prime Minister</a> (<i>miniszterelnök</i>) is elected by the National Assembly, serving as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and exercising <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a>. Traditionally, the Prime Minister is the leader of the largest party in parliament. The Prime Minister selects <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Hungary" title="Government of Hungary">Cabinet</a> ministers and has the exclusive right to dismiss them, although cabinet nominees must appear before consultative open hearings before one or more parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Committee" title="Committee">committees</a>, survive a vote in the National Assembly, and be formally approved by the president. The cabinet reports to <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Hungary)" title="National Assembly (Hungary)">parliament</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2009 Hungary, due to strong economic difficulties, had to request the help of the IMF for about €9&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Debt-to-GDP_ratio" title="Debt-to-GDP ratio">debt-to-GDP ratio</a> of Hungary had its peak in 2011 when it stood at 83% and decreased since then. According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">government gross debt</a> of Hungary amounts to 25.119&nbsp;billion HUF or 74.1% of its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> The government achieved a budget deficit 1.9% of the GDP in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Hungary's <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a> by <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating_agencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Credit rating agencies">credit rating agencies</a> <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Moody's">Moody's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch Ratings</a> stands at Investment Grade <i>BBB</i> with a stable outlook in 2016. </p>
      <p>On <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s 2019 <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> Hungary's <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> has deteriorated from a score of 51 in 2015 to 44 in 2019 making it the 2nd most corrupt EU member at pair with Romania and behind Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following a decade of <a href="/wiki/Fidesz" title="Fidesz">Fidesz</a>-<a href="/wiki/KDNP" class="mw-redirect" title="KDNP">KDNP</a> rule lead by <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orbán">Viktor Orbán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>'s <i>Nations in Transit 2020</i> report reclassified Hungary from a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> to a transitional or <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a>. According to the report, "the right-wing alliance... has gradually undermined the rule of law in Hungary and established tight control over the country’s independent institutions... [it] has steadily rewritten the Hungarian constitution, and eliminated democratic safeguards statutorily embodied in the Constitutional Court, Prosecutors Office, Media Authority, and State Audit Office...". It also limited parliamentary oversight, independent <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">media</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organizations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academic_freedom" title="Academic freedom">academics</a>, while consolidating power around the central government.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> </p>

      </div>
