      <p>Since the fall of communism, Hungary has a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2018_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="2018 Hungarian parliamentary election">last Hungarian parliamentary election</a> took place on 8 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> This parliamentary election was the 7th since the <a href="/wiki/1990_Hungarian_parliamentary_election" title="1990 Hungarian parliamentary election">1990 first multi-party election</a>. The result was a victory for <a href="/wiki/Fidesz" title="Fidesz">Fidesz</a>–<a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_(Hungary)" title="Christian Democratic People's Party (Hungary)">KDNP</a> alliance, preserving its two-thirds majority with <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orbán">Viktor Orbán</a> remaining Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> It was the second election according to the new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Hungary" title="Constitution of Hungary">Constitution of Hungary</a> which went into force on 1 January 2012. The new electoral law also entered into force that day. The voters elected 199 MPs instead of previous 386 lawmakers.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> The current political landscape in Hungary is dominated by the conservative <a href="/wiki/Fidesz" title="Fidesz">Fidesz</a>, who have a near supermajority, and two medium-sized parties, the left-wing <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Coalition_(Hungary)" title="Democratic Coalition (Hungary)">Democratic Coalition</a> (DK) and liberal <a href="/wiki/Momentum_Movement" title="Momentum Movement">Momentum</a>. </p>
      <p>The democratic character of the Hungarian parliament was reestablished with <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">the fall of the Iron Curtain</a> and the end of communist dictatorship in 1989. Today's parliament is still called <i>Országgyűlés</i> just like in royal times, but in order to differentiate between the historical royal diet is referred to as the "National Assembly" now. The <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_Hungary" title="Diet of Hungary">Diet of Hungary</a> was a legislative institution in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_in_the_Middle_Ages" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Hungary in the Middle Ages">medieval kingdom of Hungary</a> from the 1290s,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> and in its successor states, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Hungary">Royal Hungary</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lands_of_the_Crown_of_Saint_Stephen" title="Lands of the Crown of Saint Stephen">Habsburg kingdom of Hungary</a> throughout the <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern period">Early Modern period</a>. The articles of the 1790 diet set out that the diet should meet at least once every 3 years, but, since the diet was called by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg monarchy">Habsburg monarchy</a>, this promise was not kept on several occasions thereafter. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Compromise_of_1867" title="Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867">Austro-Hungarian Compromise</a>, it was reconstituted in 1867. The Latin term <i>Natio Hungarica</i> ("Hungarian nation") was used to designate the political elite which had participation in the diet, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_nobility" title="Hungarian nobility">nobility</a>, the Catholic clergy, and a few enfranchised burghers,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> regardless of language or ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_judicial_system">Law and judicial system</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Hungary" title="Law of Hungary">Law of Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Hungary" title="Law enforcement in Hungary">Law enforcement in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG/220px-NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG/330px-NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG/440px-NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="1636"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NeprajziMuzeumFotoThalerTamas1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The original and the future seat of The Curia, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">highest court</a> in Hungary
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The judicial system of Hungary is a <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> system divided between <a href="/wiki/Court" title="Court">courts</a> with regular civil and criminal jurisdiction and <a href="/wiki/Administrative_court" title="Administrative court">administrative courts</a> with jurisdiction over litigation between individuals and the public administration. Hungarian law is codified and based on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Germany" title="Law of Germany">German law</a> and in a wider sense, civil law or <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a>. The court system for civil and criminal jurisdiction consists of local courts (<i>járásbíróság</i>), regional appellate courts (<i>ítélőtábla</i>), and the supreme court (<i>Kúria</i>). Hungary's highest <a href="/wiki/Court" title="Court">courts</a> are located in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Law enforcement in Hungary is split among the <a href="/wiki/Rend%C5%91rs%C3%A9g" title="Rendőrség">police</a> and the National Tax and Customs Administration. The Hungarian Police is the main and largest state <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency" title="Law enforcement agency">law enforcement agency</a> in Hungary. It carries nearly all general police duties such as criminal investigation, patrol activity, traffic policing, border control. It is led by the National Police Commissioner under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Hungary)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Interior (Hungary)">Minister of the Interior</a>. The body is divided into county police departments which are also divided into regional and town police departments. The National Police also have subordinate agencies with nationwide jurisdiction, such as the "Nemzeti Nyomozó Iroda" (National Bureau of Investigation), a civilian police force specialised in investigating serious crimes, and the gendarmerie-like, militarised "Készenléti Rendőrség" (Stand-by Police) mainly dealing with riots and often reinforcing local police forces. Due to Hungary's accession to the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Schengen Treaty">Schengen Treaty</a>, the Police and Border Guards were merged into a single national corps, with the Border Guards becoming Police Officers. This merger took place in January 2008. The Customs and Excise Authority remained subject to the Ministry of Finance under the National Tax and Customs Administration.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Hungary" title="Administrative divisions of Hungary">Administrative divisions of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state nation</a> divided into 19 <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Hungary" title="Counties of Hungary">counties</a> (<i>megye</i>). In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Capitals_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitals of Hungary">capital</a> (<i>főváros</i>), <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, is an independent entity. The counties and the capital are the 20 <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">NUTS</a> third-level units of Hungary. The states are further subdivided into 174 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Hungary" title="Districts of Hungary">districts</a> (<i>járás</i>) as of 1&nbsp;January&nbsp;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hungary&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> The districts are further divided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_of_Hungary" title="List of cities and towns of Hungary">towns and villages</a>, of which 23 are designated <a href="/wiki/Town_with_county_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Town with county rights">towns with county rights</a> (<i>megyei jogú város</i>), sometimes known as "urban counties" in English. The local authorities of these towns have extended powers, but these towns belong to the territory of the respective district instead of being independent territorial units. County and district councils and municipalities have different roles and separate responsibilities relating to local government. The role of the counties are basically administrative and focus on strategic development, while preschools, public water utilities, garbage disposal, elderly care, and rescue services are administered by the municipalities. </p>
      <p>Since 1996, the counties and City of Budapest have been grouped into seven <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Regions of Hungary">regions</a> for statistical and development purposes. These seven regions constitute <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">NUTS</a>' second-level units of Hungary. They are <a href="/wiki/Central_Hungary" title="Central Hungary">Central Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Transdanubia" title="Central Transdanubia">Central Transdanubia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Great_Plain" title="Northern Great Plain">Northern Great Plain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hungary" title="Northern Hungary">Northern Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Transdanubia" title="Southern Transdanubia">Southern Transdanubia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Great_Plain" title="Southern Great Plain">Southern Great Plain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Transdanubia" title="Western Transdanubia">Western Transdanubia</a>. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Hungary" title="Foreign relations of Hungary">Foreign relations of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Necasmeeting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Necasmeeting.jpg/220px-Necasmeeting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Necasmeeting.jpg/330px-Necasmeeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Necasmeeting.jpg/440px-Necasmeeting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1417" data-file-height="945"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Necasmeeting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Meeting of <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> leaders, plus Germany and France in 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg/220px-BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg/330px-BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg/440px-BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BIMUN_2012_opening_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> conference in the assembly hall of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Magnates" title="House of Magnates">House of Magnates</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Parliament_Building" title="Hungarian Parliament Building">Hungarian Parliament</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> of Hungary is based on four basic commitments: to <a href="/wiki/Atlanticism" title="Atlanticism">Atlantic co-operation</a>, to <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>, to <a href="/wiki/International_development" title="International development">international development</a> and to <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Hungary" title="Economy of Hungary">Hungarian economy</a> is fairly open<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2021)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and relies strongly on <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Hungary has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since December 1955 and a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank" title="Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank">AIIB</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>. Hungary took on the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> for half a year in 2011 and the next will be in 2024. In 2015, Hungary was the fifth largest <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> Non-DAC donor of <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a> in the world, which represents <a href="/wiki/List_of_development_aid_country_donors" title="List of development aid country donors">0.13% of its Gross National Income</a>. </p>
      <p>Hungary's capital city, Budapest, is home to more than 100 embassies and representative bodies as an international political actor.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> Hungary hosts the main and regional headquarters of many international organisations as well, including <a href="/wiki/European_Institute_of_Innovation_and_Technology" title="European Institute of Innovation and Technology">European Institute of Innovation and Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Police_College" class="mw-redirect" title="European Police College">European Police College</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_of_the_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations">Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Democratic_Transition" title="International Centre for Democratic Transition">International Centre for Democratic Transition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_International_Education" title="Institute of International Education">Institute of International Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">International Red Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regional_Environmental_Center_for_Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Regional Environmental Center for Central and Eastern Europe">Regional Environmental Center for Central and Eastern Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danube_Commission_(1948)" title="Danube Commission (1948)">Danube Commission</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 1989, Hungary's top foreign policy goal has been achieving integration into Western economic and security organisations. Hungary joined the <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> programme in 1994 and has actively supported the <a href="/wiki/IFOR" class="mw-redirect" title="IFOR">IFOR</a> and <a href="/wiki/SFOR" class="mw-redirect" title="SFOR">SFOR</a> missions in Bosnia. Hungary since 1989 has also improved its often frosty neighbourly relations by signing basic treaties with <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>. These renounce all outstanding territorial claims and lay the foundation for constructive relations. However, the issue of <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">ethnic Hungarian minority</a> rights in Romania, Slovakia, and Serbia periodically cause bilateral tensions to flare up. Since 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Hungary%E2%80%93Ukraine_relations" title="Hungary–Ukraine relations">relations with Ukraine</a> rapidly deteriorated over the issue of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Ukraine" title="Hungarians in Ukraine">Hungarian minority in Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> Hungary since 1989 has signed all of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a> documents, and served as the OSCE's Chairman-in-Office in 1997. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Defence_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Defence Force">Hungarian Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Hungary" title="List of heads of state of Hungary">President</a> holds the title of <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the nation's armed forces. The <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Defence_(Hungary)" title="Minister of Defence (Hungary)">Ministry of Defence</a> jointly with <a href="/wiki/General_Staff_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_the_Republic_of_Hungary" title="General Staff of the Armed Forces of the Republic of Hungary">Chief of staff</a> administers the armed forces, including the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Ground_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Ground Force">Hungarian Ground Force</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Air_Force" title="Hungarian Air Force">Hungarian Air Force</a>. Since 2007, the Hungarian Armed Forces has been under a unified command structure. The Ministry of Defence maintains political and civil control over the army. A subordinate Joint Forces Command coordinates and commands the HDF. In 2016, the armed forces had 31,080 personnel on active duty, the operative reserve brought the total number of troops to fifty thousand. In 2016, it was planned that military spending the following year would be $1.21&nbsp;billion, about 0.94% of the country's GDP, well below the NATO target of 2%. In 2012, the government adopted a resolution in which it pledged to increase defence spending to 1.4% of GDP by 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hunspec.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Hunspec.jpg/220px-Hunspec.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Hunspec.jpg/330px-Hunspec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Hunspec.jpg/440px-Hunspec.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="961"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hunspec.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/HDF_34th_Bercs%C3%A9nyi_L%C3%A1szl%C3%B3_Special_Forces_Battalion" title="HDF 34th Bercsényi László Special Forces Battalion">HDF 34th Special Forces Battalion</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG/220px-JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG/330px-JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG/440px-JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1548" data-file-height="1031"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:JAS_39_pair_HuAF_Kecskem%C3%A9t_2007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/JAS_39_Gripen" class="mw-redirect" title="JAS 39 Gripen">JAS 39 Gripen</a> <a href="/wiki/Multirole_combat_aircraft" title="Multirole combat aircraft">multirole combat aircraft</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">Military service</a> is voluntary, though <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> may occur in wartime. In a significant move for modernisation, Hungary decided in 2001 to buy 14 <a href="/wiki/JAS_39_Gripen" class="mw-redirect" title="JAS 39 Gripen">JAS 39 Gripen</a> fighter aircraft for about 800&nbsp;million EUR. Hungarian National Cyber Security Center was re-organised in 2016 in order to become more efficient through <a href="/wiki/Cyber_security" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber security">cyber security</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2016, the Hungarian military had about 700 troops stationed in foreign countries as part of international peacekeeping forces, including 100 HDF troops in the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-led <a href="/wiki/ISAF" class="mw-redirect" title="ISAF">ISAF</a> force in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, 210 Hungarian soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> under command of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a>, and 160 troops in <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>. Hungary sent a 300-strong logistics unit to Iraq in order to help the US occupation with armed transport convoys, though public opinion opposed the country's participation in the war.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Hungary" title="Economy of Hungary">Economy of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:EU_Single_Market.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EU_Single_Market.svg/220px-EU_Single_Market.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EU_Single_Market.svg/330px-EU_Single_Market.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EU_Single_Market.svg/440px-EU_Single_Market.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:EU_Single_Market.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hungary is part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Internal_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal market">internal market</a> with 508&nbsp;million consumers and part of <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg/220px-Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg/330px-Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg/440px-Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hungary_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hungary's Export Treemap from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://atlas.cid.harvard.edu/explore/tree_map/export/hun/all/show/2014/">Harvard Economic Complexity Observatory</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary is an <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> <a href="/wiki/High-income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income economy">high-income</a> <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> with <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">very high human development index</a> and skilled <a href="/wiki/Labour_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour force">labour force</a> with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">16th lowest income inequality</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Furthermore, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_complexity" title="List of countries by economic complexity">9th most complex economy</a> according to the Economic Complexity Index.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> The Hungarian is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">57th-largest economy in the world</a> (out of 188 countries measured by <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a>) with $265.037&nbsp;billion output,<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-160">[159]</a></sup> and ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">49th in the world in terms of GDP per capita</a> measured by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. Hungary is an export-oriented <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> with a heavy emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Foreign_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign trade">foreign trade</a>, thus the country is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">36th largest export economy</a> in the world. The country has more than $100&nbsp;billion export in 2015 with high, $9.003&nbsp;billion <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">trade surplus</a>, of which 79% went to the EU and 21% was extra-EU trade.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> Hungary has a more than 80% <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">privately owned</a> economy with <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_tax_revenue_as_percentage_of_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by tax revenue as percentage of GDP">39,1% overall taxation</a>, which provides the basis for the country's <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare economy</a>. On the expenditure side, <a href="/wiki/Household_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Household consumption">household consumption</a> is the main component of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> and accounts for 50 percent of its total use, followed by gross fixed <a href="/wiki/Capital_formation" title="Capital formation">capital formation</a> with 22 percent and <a href="/wiki/Government_expenditure" class="mw-redirect" title="Government expenditure">government expenditure</a> with 20 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> Hungary continues to be one of the leading nations for attracting <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>, the inward FDI in the country was $119.8&nbsp;billion in 2015, while Hungary invests more than $50&nbsp;billion abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hungary&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the key trading partners of Hungary were Germany, Austria, Romania, Slovakia, France, Italy, Poland and Czech Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> Major industries include food processing, pharmaceuticals, motor vehicles, information technology, chemicals, metallurgy, machinery, electrical goods, and tourism (in 2014 Hungary welcomed 12.1&nbsp;million international tourists).<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> Hungary is the largest electronics producer in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>. <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">Electronics</a> manufacturing and research are among the main drivers of <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a> and economic growth in the country. In the past 20 years Hungary has also grown into a major centre for <a href="/wiki/Mobile_technology" title="Mobile technology">mobile technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a>, and related hardware research.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Employment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Employment rate">employment rate</a> in the economy was 68.3% in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> the employment structure shows the characteristics of <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial economies</a>, 63.2% of employed workforce work in service sector, the industry contributed by 29.7%, while agriculture with 7.1%. Unemployment rate was 4.1% in 2017 September,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> down from 11% during the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">financial crisis of 2007–08</a>. Hungary is part of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal market">European single market</a> which represents more than 508&nbsp;million consumers. Several domestic commercial policies are determined by agreements among European Union members and by EU legislation. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg/220px-Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg/330px-Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg/440px-Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3580" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9chenyi_Chain_Bridge_in_Budapest_at_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> is a leading <a href="/wiki/R%26D" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;D">R&amp;D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial center">financial center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Large <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Hungary" title="List of companies of Hungary">Hungarian companies</a> are included in the <a href="/wiki/BUX" title="BUX">BUX</a>, the Hungarian stock market index listed on <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Stock_Exchange" title="Budapest Stock Exchange">Budapest Stock Exchange</a>. Well-known companies include the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> firm <a href="/wiki/MOL_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="MOL Group">MOL Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/OTP_Bank" title="OTP Bank">OTP Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gedeon_Richter_Plc." class="mw-redirect" title="Gedeon Richter Plc.">Gedeon Richter Plc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magyar_Telekom" title="Magyar Telekom">Magyar Telekom</a>, <a href="/wiki/CIG_Pannonia" title="CIG Pannonia">CIG Pannonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/FHB_Mortgage_Bank" title="FHB Mortgage Bank">FHB Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zwack_liqueur" class="mw-redirect" title="Zwack liqueur">Zwack Unicum</a> and more.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> Besides this Hungary has a large portion of specialised <a href="/wiki/Small_and_medium_enterprise" class="mw-redirect" title="Small and medium enterprise">small and medium enterprise</a>, for example a significant number of automotive suppliers and technology <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">start ups</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> is the financial and business capital of Hungary. The capital is a significant economic hub, classified as an Alpha – <a href="/wiki/World_city" class="mw-redirect" title="World city">world city</a> in the study by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network</a> and it is the second fastest-developing <a href="/wiki/Urban_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban economy">urban economy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> as GDP per capita in the city increased by 2.4 per cent and employment by 4.7 per cent compared to the previous year in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> On the national level, Budapest is the <a href="/wiki/Primate_city" title="Primate city">primate city</a> of Hungary regarding business and economy, accounting for 39% of the national income, the city has a <a href="/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product" title="Gross metropolitan product">gross metropolitan product</a> more than $100&nbsp;billion in 2015, making it one of the largest regional economies in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> Budapest is also among the Top 100 GDP performing cities in the world, measured by <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> and in a global city competitiveness ranking by <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">EIU</a>, Budapest stands before <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> Furthermore, Hungary's corporate tax rate is only 9%, which is relatively low for EU states.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Hungary maintains its own currency, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_forint" title="Hungarian forint">Hungarian forint</a> (HUF), although the economy fulfills the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_criteria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maastricht criteria">Maastricht criteria</a> with the exception of public debt, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_public_debt" title="List of countries by public debt">but it is also significantly below the EU average</a> with the level of 75.3% in 2015. The <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_National_Bank" title="Hungarian National Bank">Hungarian National Bank</a>—founded in 1924, after the dissolution of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>—is currently focusing on price stability with an inflation target of 3%.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Hungary" title="Science and technology in Hungary">Science and technology in Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Hungary" title="Education in Hungary">Education in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg/220px-Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg/330px-Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg/440px-Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1118" data-file-height="817"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Szentgyorgyi_Albert_es_a_c_vitamin_keplete_1937_okt_31_Pesti_Naplo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Albert_Szent-Gy%C3%B6rgyi" title="Albert Szent-Györgyi">Albert Szent-Györgyi</a> a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Laureate in Medicine</a> for discovery of <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">Vitamin C</a>. Nobel Prize has been awarded to <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hungarian_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Hungarian Nobel laureates">13 Hungarian laureates</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg/220px-Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg/330px-Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg/440px-Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3493" data-file-height="1917"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Budapesti_M%C5%B1szaki_Egyetem_K_%C3%A9p%C3%BClet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Budapest_University_of_Technology_and_Economics" title="Budapest University of Technology and Economics">Budapest University of Technology and Economics</a> is the oldest operational <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">Institute of technology</a> in the world, founded in 1782
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary's achievements in <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> have been significant, and <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> efforts form an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Hungary" title="Economy of Hungary">country's economy</a>. Hungary spent 1.4% of its gross domestic product (GDP) on civil <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> in 2015, which is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_research_and_development_spending" title="List of countries by research and development spending">25th highest ratio in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-179">[178]</a></sup> Hungary ranks 32nd among the most innovative countries in the <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Innovation_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloomberg Innovation Index">Bloomberg Innovation Index</a>, standing before <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> or <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> places Hungary 33rd among the countries of the world in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> In 2014, Hungary counted 2,651 full-time equivalent researchers per million inhabitants, steadily increasing from 2,131 in 2010 and compares with 3,984 in the US or 4,380 in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> Hungary's <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high technology</a> industry has benefited from both the country's skilled workforce and the strong presence of foreign high-tech firms and <a href="/wiki/Research_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Research center">research centres</a>. Hungary also has one of the highest rates of filed <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a>, the sixth highest ratio of high-tech and medium high-tech output in the total industrial output, the 12th highest research <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">FDI</a> inflow, placed 14th in research talent in business enterprise and has the 17th best overall innovation efficiency ratio in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The key actor of research and development in Hungary is the National Research, Development and Innovation Office (NRDI Office), which is a national strategic and <a href="/wiki/Funding_of_science" title="Funding of science">funding agency for scientific research, development and innovation</a>, the primary source of advice on RDI policy for the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Hungary" title="Government of Hungary">Hungarian Government</a>, and the primary RDI funding agency. Its role is to develop RDI policy and ensure that Hungary adequately invest in RDI by funding excellent research and supporting innovation to increase competitiveness and to prepare the RDI strategy of the Hungarian Government, to handle the National Research, Development and Innovation Fund, and represents the Hungarian Government and a Hungarian RDI community in international organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg/220px-Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg/330px-Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg/440px-Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="711"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Richter-Gedeon-Nyrt-P5010610.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">Research and development</a> centre of <a href="/wiki/Gedeon_Richter_Plc." class="mw-redirect" title="Gedeon Richter Plc.">Gedeon Richter Plc.</a> in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> company in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Scientific research in the country is supported partly by industry and partly by the state, through the <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="List of universities in Hungary">network of Hungarian universities</a> and by scientific state-institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Hungarian Academy of Sciences">Hungarian Academy of Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> Hungary has been the home of some of the most prominent researchers in various scientific disciplines, notably <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>. As of 2018, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hungarian_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Hungarian Nobel laureates">twelve Hungarian scientists</a> have been recipients of a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup> Until 2012 three individuals: Csoma, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Bolyai" title="János Bolyai">János Bolyai</a> and Tihanyi were included in the UNESCO Memory of the world register as well as the collective contributions: <a href="/wiki/Tabula_Hungariae" title="Tabula Hungariae">Tabula Hungariae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bibliotheca_Corviniana" title="Bibliotheca Corviniana">Bibliotheca Corviniana</a>. Contemporary, internationally well-known Hungarian scientists include mathematician <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A1szl%C3%B3_Lov%C3%A1sz" title="László Lovász">László Lovász</a>, physicist <a href="/wiki/Albert-L%C3%A1szl%C3%B3_Barab%C3%A1si" title="Albert-László Barabási">Albert-László Barabási</a>, physicist <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Krausz" title="Ferenc Krausz">Ferenc Krausz</a>, and biochemist <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d_Pusztai" title="Árpád Pusztai">Árpád Pusztai</a>. Hungary is famous for its excellent <a href="/wiki/Mathematics_education" title="Mathematics education">mathematics education</a> which has trained numerous outstanding scientists. Famous Hungarian mathematicians include father <a href="/wiki/Farkas_Bolyai" title="Farkas Bolyai">Farkas Bolyai</a> and son <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Bolyai" title="János Bolyai">János Bolyai</a>, who was one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/Non-Euclidean_geometry" title="Non-Euclidean geometry">non-Euclidean geometry</a>; <a href="/wiki/Paul_Erd%C5%91s" title="Paul Erdős">Paul Erdős</a>, famed for publishing in over forty languages and whose <a href="/wiki/Erd%C5%91s_number" title="Erdős number">Erdős numbers</a> are still tracked, and <a href="/wiki/John_von_Neumann" title="John von Neumann">John von Neumann</a>, a key contributor in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Game_theory" title="Game theory">game theory</a>, a pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Digital_computing" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital computing">digital computing</a>, and the chief mathematician in the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>. Notable Hungarian inventions include the <a href="/wiki/Lead_dioxide" title="Lead dioxide">lead dioxide</a> <a href="/wiki/Match" title="Match">match</a> (<a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Irinyi" title="János Irinyi">János Irinyi</a>), a type of <a href="/wiki/Carburetor" title="Carburetor">carburetor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Don%C3%A1t_B%C3%A1nki" title="Donát Bánki">Donát Bánki</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Csonka" title="János Csonka">János Csonka</a>), the electric (AC) train engine and generator (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_Kand%C3%B3" title="Kálmán Kandó">Kálmán Kandó</a>), <a href="/wiki/Holography" title="Holography">holography</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dennis_Gabor" title="Dennis Gabor">Dennis Gabor</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Kalman_filter" title="Kalman filter">Kalman filter</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rudolf_E._K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n" title="Rudolf E. Kálmán">Rudolf E. Kálmán</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Rubik%27s_Cube" title="Rubik's Cube">Rubik's Cube</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ern%C5%91_Rubik" title="Ernő Rubik">Ernő Rubik</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Hungary" title="Transport in Hungary">Transport in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Esztergom.desiro.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Esztergom.desiro.JPG/220px-Esztergom.desiro.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Esztergom.desiro.JPG/330px-Esztergom.desiro.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Esztergom.desiro.JPG/440px-Esztergom.desiro.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2271" data-file-height="1088"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Esztergom.desiro.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Siemens_Desiro" title="Siemens Desiro">Siemens Desiro</a> on <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_State_Railways" title="Hungarian State Railways">Hungarian State Railways</a> network, which is <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_rail_transport_network_size" title="List of countries by rail transport network size">one of the densest in the world</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary has a highly developed road, railway, air, and water transport system. Budapest, the capital, serves as an important hub for the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_State_Railways" title="Hungarian State Railways">Hungarian railway system</a> (<i>MÁV</i>). The capital is served by three large train stations called <i><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Railway_Station_(Budapest)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Railway Station (Budapest)">Keleti</a></i> (Eastern), <i><a href="/wiki/Western_Railway_Station_(Budapest)" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Railway Station (Budapest)">Nyugati</a></i> (Western), and <i><a href="/wiki/Southern_Railway_Station_(Budapest)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Railway Station (Budapest)">Déli</a></i> (Southern) <i>pályaudvar</i>s. <a href="/wiki/Szolnok" title="Szolnok">Szolnok</a> is the most important railway hub outside Budapest, while <a href="/wiki/Tiszai_Railway_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiszai Railway Station">Tiszai Railway Station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miskolc" title="Miskolc">Miskolc</a> and the main stations of <a href="/wiki/Szombathely" title="Szombathely">Szombathely</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gy%C5%91r" title="Győr">Győr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Szeged" title="Szeged">Szeged</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kesfeh%C3%A9rv%C3%A1r" title="Székesfehérvár">Székesfehérvár</a> are also key to the network. </p>
      <p>Budapest, <a href="/wiki/Debrecen" title="Debrecen">Debrecen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miskolc" title="Miskolc">Miskolc</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Szeged" title="Szeged">Szeged</a> have tram networks. The <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Metro" title="Budapest Metro">Budapest Metro</a> is the second-oldest underground <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system in the world; its <a href="/wiki/Line_1_(Budapest_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Line 1 (Budapest Metro)">Line 1</a> dates from 1896. The system consists of four lines. A <a href="/wiki/Regional_rail" title="Regional rail">commuter rail</a> system, <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%89V" class="mw-redirect" title="HÉV">HÉV</a></i>, operates in the Budapest metropolitan area. Hungary has a total length of approximately 1,314&nbsp;km (816.48&nbsp;mi) motorways (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">autópálya</i>). Motorway sections are being added to the existing network, which already connects many major economically important cities to the capital. The most important port is Budapest. Other important ones include <a href="/wiki/Duna%C3%BAjv%C3%A1ros" title="Dunaújváros">Dunaújváros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baja,_Hungary" title="Baja, Hungary">Baja</a>. </p>
      <p>There are five international airports in Hungary: <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Liszt_Ferenc_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Budapest Liszt Ferenc International Airport">Budapest Liszt Ferenc</a> (informally called "Ferihegy" after its previous name), <a href="/wiki/Debrecen_International_Airport" title="Debrecen International Airport">Debrecen</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1rmell%C3%A9k_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Sármellék International Airport">Sármellék</a> (also called Hévíz-Balaton Airport), <a href="/wiki/Gy%C5%91r-P%C3%A9r_International_Airport" title="Győr-Pér International Airport">Győr-Pér</a>, and <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9cs-Pog%C3%A1ny_International_Airport" title="Pécs-Pogány International Airport">Pécs-Pogány</a>. The national carrier, <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Hungarian_Airlines" title="Malév Hungarian Airlines">MALÉV</a>, operated flights to over 60, mostly European cities, but ceased operations in 2012. Low-budget airline <a href="/wiki/WizzAir" class="mw-redirect" title="WizzAir">WizzAir</a> is based in Hungary, at Ferihegy. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Hungary" title="Demographics of Hungary">Demographics of Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Hungary" title="Women in Hungary">Women in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_density_in_Hungary.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Population_density_in_Hungary.png/290px-Population_density_in_Hungary.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Population_density_in_Hungary.png/435px-Population_density_in_Hungary.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Population_density_in_Hungary.png/580px-Population_density_in_Hungary.png 2x" data-file-width="870" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_density_in_Hungary.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population density in Hungary by <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Hungary" title="Districts of Hungary">district</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary's population was 9,937,628 according to the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a>, making it the fifth most populous country in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_European_Union" title="Demographics of the European Union">medium-sized member state of the European Union</a>. <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">Population density</a> stands at 107 inhabitants per square kilometre, which is about two times higher than the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">world average</a>. More than one quarter of the population lived in the <a href="/wiki/Budapest_metropolitan_area" title="Budapest metropolitan area">Budapest metropolitan area</a>, 6,903,858 people (69.5%) in <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_of_Hungary" title="List of cities and towns of Hungary">cities and towns</a> overall.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-188">[187]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Like most other European countries, Hungary is experiencing <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">sub-replacement fertility</a>; its estimated <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of 1.43 children per woman is well below the replacement rate of 2.1,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> albeit higher than its nadir of 1.28 in 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> and remains considerably below the high of 5.59 children born per woman in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> As a result, its population has been gradually declining and rapidly ageing. In 2011, the conservative government began a programme to increase the birth rate with a focus on ethnic Magyars by reinstating 3 year maternity leave as well as boosting part-time jobs. The fertility rate has gradually increased from 1.27 children born/woman in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> The natural decrease in the first 10 months of 2016 was only 25,828 which was 8,162 less than the corresponding period in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> In 2015, 47.9% of births were to unmarried women.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> Hungary has one of the oldest populations in the world, with the average age of 42.7 years.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> was 71.96 years for men and 79.62 years for women in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> growing continuously since the <a href="/wiki/End_of_Communism_in_Hungary_(1989)" class="mw-redirect" title="End of Communism in Hungary (1989)">fall of Communism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Hungary recognises two sizeable minority groups, designated as "national minorities" because their ancestors have lived in their respective regions for centuries in Hungary: a <a href="/wiki/Germans_of_Hungary" title="Germans of Hungary">German community</a> of about 130,000 that lives throughout the country, and a <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Hungary" title="Romani people in Hungary">Romani minority</a> numerous around 300,000 that mainly resides in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hungary" title="Northern Hungary">the northern part of the country</a>. Some studies indicate a considerably larger number of Romani in Hungary (876,000 people – c. 9% of the population.).<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> According to the 2011 census, there were 8,314,029 (83.7%) ethnic <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a>, 308,957 (3.1%) <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>, 131,951 (1.3%) <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, 29,647 (0.3%) <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>, 26,345 (0.3%) <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, and 23,561 (0.2%) <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a> in Hungary; 1,455,883 people (14.7% of the total population) did not declare their ethnicity. Thus, Hungarians made up more than 90% of people who declared their ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011det_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011det-5">[4]</a></sup> In Hungary, people can declare more than one ethnicity, so the sum of ethnicities is higher than the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today approximately <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">5&nbsp;million Hungarians live outside Hungary</a>. </p>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hungary_local_administration.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hungary_local_administration.png/290px-Hungary_local_administration.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hungary_local_administration.png/435px-Hungary_local_administration.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hungary_local_administration.png/580px-Hungary_local_administration.png 2x" data-file-width="1601" data-file-height="1025"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hungary_local_administration.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Towns and villages in Hungary
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary has 3,152 localities as of 15 July 2013. 346 towns (Hungarian term: <i>város</i>, plural: <i>városok</i>; the terminology doesn't distinguish between <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">towns</a> – the term town is used in official translations) and 2,806 villages (Hungarian: <i>község</i>, plural: <i>községek</i>). The number of towns can change, since villages can be elevated to town status by act of the President. The capital Budapest has a special status and is not included in any county while 23 of the towns are so-called urban counties (<i>megyei jogú város</i> – town with county rights). All county seats except Budapest are urban counties. </p>
      <p>Four of the cities (<a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miskolc" title="Miskolc">Miskolc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gy%C5%91r" title="Győr">Győr</a>, and <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9cs" title="Pécs">Pécs</a>) have agglomerations, and the Hungarian Statistical Office distinguishes seventeen other areas in earlier stages of agglomeration development.<sup id="cite_ref-portal_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portal-201">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The largest city is the capital, Budapest, the smallest town is <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1lh%C3%A1za" title="Pálháza">Pálháza</a> with 1038 inhabitants (2010). The largest village is <a href="/wiki/Solym%C3%A1r" title="Solymár">Solymár</a> (population: 10,123 as of 2010) There are more than 100 villages with fewer than 100 inhabitants while the smallest villages have fewer than 20 inhabitants. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Hungary" title="Languages of Hungary">Languages of Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg/290px-Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg/435px-Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg/580px-Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="688" data-file-height="438"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dist_of_hu_lang_europe.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Present-day regions in Europe where Hungarian is the majority language
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official</a> and predominant spoken language in Hungary. Hungarian is the <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Europe" title="Languages of Europe">13th most widely spoken first language in Europe</a> with around 13&nbsp;million native speakers and it is one of 24 official and working languages of the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> Outside Hungary it is also spoken by communities of Hungarian people in neighbouring countries and by <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">Hungarian diaspora</a> communities worldwide. According to the 2011 census, 9,896,333 people (99.6%) speak Hungarian in Hungary, of whom 9,827,875 people (99%) speak it as a <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a>, while 68,458 people (0.7%) speak it as a <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">second language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011det_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011det-5">[4]</a></sup> English (1,589,180 speakers, 16.0%), and German (1,111,997 speakers, 11.2%) are the most widely spoken <a href="/wiki/Foreign_language" title="Foreign language">foreign languages</a>, while there are several recognised minority languages in Hungary (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">Rusyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovenian language">Slovenian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-188">[187]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Hungarian (Magyar) is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic language family</a>, unrelated to any neighbouring language and distantly related to <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>. It is the largest of the Uralic languages in terms of the number of speakers and the only one spoken in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. There are sizeable populations of Hungarian speakers in Romania, Czechia, Slovakia, the former Yugoslavia, Ukraine, Israel, and the U.S. Smaller groups of Hungarian speakers live in Canada, Slovenia, and Austria, but also in Australia, Brazil, Argentina, Mexico, Venezuela, and Chile. Standard Hungarian is based on the variety spoken in the capital of <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, although the use of the standard dialect is enforced, Hungarian has a number of urban and rural <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Hungary" title="Religion in Hungary">Religion in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary is a historically <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> country. Hungarian historiography identifies the foundation of the Hungarian state with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">Stephen I's</a> <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a> and coronation with the <a href="/wiki/Szentkorona" class="mw-redirect" title="Szentkorona">Holy Crown</a> in A.D. 1000. Stephen promulgated <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> as the state religion, and his successors were traditionally known as the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Apostolic King">Apostolic Kings</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Hungary" title="Catholic Church in Hungary">Catholic Church in Hungary</a> remained strong through the centuries, and the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Esztergom" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishop of Esztergom">Archbishop of Esztergom</a> was granted extraordinary temporal privileges as <a href="/wiki/Prince-primate" title="Prince-primate">prince-primate</a> (<i>hercegprímás</i>) of Hungary. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg/220px-Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="317" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg/330px-Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg/440px-Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1796" data-file-height="2585"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bencz%C3%BAr_-_Painting_of_St_Stephen_in_the_Basilica_of_Budapest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">King Saint Stephen</a> offering the Hungarian crown to <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Virgin Mary</a> - painting by Gyula Benczúr, in the St. Stephen's Basilica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although contemporary Hungary has no <a href="/wiki/Official_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Official religion">official religion</a> and recognises <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> as a fundamental right, the Hungarian constitution "recognizes Christianity's nation-building role" in its preamble<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> and in Article VII affirms that "the state may cooperate with the churches for community goals."<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2011 census showed that the majority of Hungarians were Christians (54.2%), with <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Hungary" title="Catholic Church in Hungary">Roman Catholics</a> (<i>Katolikusok</i>) (37.1%) and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Reformed">Hungarian Reformed</a> <a href="/wiki/Calvinist" class="mw-redirect" title="Calvinist">Calvinists</a> (<i>Reformátusok</i>) (11.1%) making up the bulk of these alongside <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a> (<i>Evangélikusok</i>) (2.2%), <a href="/wiki/Greek_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Catholic">Greek Catholics</a> (1.8%), and other Christians (1.3%). <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> (0.1%), <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> (0.1%) and <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> (0.06%) communities are in the minority. 27.2% of the population did not declare a religious affiliation while 16.7% declared themselves explicitly <a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">irreligious</a>, another 1.5% <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011det_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011det-5">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the initial stages of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, most Hungarians adopted first <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Reformed_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Reformed Church">Hungarian Reformed Church</a>. In the second half of the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Jesuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a> led a <a href="/wiki/Counterreformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterreformation">Counterreformation</a> campaign and the population once again became predominantly Catholic. This campaign was only partially successful, however, and the (mainly Reformed) Hungarian nobility were able to secure freedom of worship for Christians. In practice this meant <i><a href="/wiki/Cuius_regio,_eius_religio" title="Cuius regio, eius religio">cuius regio, eius religio</a></i>; thus, most individual localities in Hungary are still identifiable as historically Catholic, Lutheran, or Reformed.
