        <a href="/wiki/File:Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg/220px-Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg/330px-Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg/440px-Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vaterpolo_Hungary_vs_Italy_semifinal_game2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hungary_men%27s_national_water_polo_team" title="Hungary men's national water polo team">Hungary men's national water polo team</a> is considered among the best in the world, holding the world record for Olympic golds and overall medals
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hungary_at_the_Olympics" title="Hungary at the Olympics">Hungarian athletes</a> have been successful contenders in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, only ten countries have won more Olympic medals than Hungary, with a total of 498 medals ranking eighth in an <a href="/wiki/All-time_Olympic_Games_medal_count" class="mw-redirect" title="All-time Olympic Games medal count">all-time Olympic Games medal count</a>. Hungary has the third-highest number of <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medal" title="Olympic medal">Olympic medals</a> per capita and second-highest number of gold medals per capita in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup> Hungary has historically excelled in Olympic water sports. In <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> the Hungarian team is the <a href="/wiki/Water_polo_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Water polo at the Summer Olympics">leading medal winner by a significant margin</a> and in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Olympic_medalists_in_swimming_(men)" title="List of Olympic medalists in swimming (men)">swimming Hungarian men</a> are fourth most successful overall, while <a href="/wiki/List_of_Olympic_medalists_in_swimming_(women)" title="List of Olympic medalists in swimming (women)">the women</a> are eighth-most successful overall. They have also seen success in canoeing and kayaking <a href="/wiki/Canoeing_and_kayaking_at_the_Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Canoeing and kayaking at the Summer Olympics">they are the third most successful overall</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Groupama_Arena_Budapest_(17267881892).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Groupama_Arena_Budapest_%2817267881892%29.jpg/220px-Groupama_Arena_Budapest_%2817267881892%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Groupama_Arena_Budapest_%2817267881892%29.jpg/330px-Groupama_Arena_Budapest_%2817267881892%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Groupama_Arena_Budapest_%2817267881892%29.jpg/440px-Groupama_Arena_Budapest_%2817267881892%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5465" data-file-height="3644"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Groupama_Arena_Budapest_(17267881892).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Groupama_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Groupama Arena">Groupama Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferencv%C3%A1rosi_TC" title="Ferencvárosi TC">Ferencvárosi TC</a>'s <a href="/wiki/UEFA_stadium_categories" title="UEFA stadium categories">UEFA category four stadium</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary won its first gold medal in Winter Olympics in 2018 in mens short track speed skating with a team of four: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hungarianfreepress.com/tag/csaba-burjan/">Csaba Burján</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hungarianfreepress.com/tag/sandor-liu/">Sándor Liu</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hungarianfreepress.com/tag/shaoang-liu/">Shaoang Liu</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hungarianfreepress.com/tag/viktor-knoch/">Viktor Knoch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015 the Assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Olympic_Committee" title="Hungarian Olympic Committee">Hungarian Olympic Committee</a> and the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_Budapest" title="General Assembly of Budapest">Assembly of Budapest</a> decided to bid for the <a href="/wiki/2024_Summer_Olympics" title="2024 Summer Olympics">2024 Summer Olympics</a> but eventually awarded to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. Budapest has also lost several bids to host the games, in <a href="/wiki/1916_Summer_Olympics" title="1916 Summer Olympics">1916</a>, <a href="/wiki/1920_Summer_Olympics" title="1920 Summer Olympics">1920</a>, <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1944_Summer_Olympics" title="1944 Summer Olympics">1944</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">1960</a> to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[248]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Hungary hosted many global <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sport</a> event in the past, among others the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Amateur_Boxing_Championships" title="1997 World Amateur Boxing Championships">1997 World Amateur Boxing Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Fencing_Championships" title="2000 World Fencing Championships">2000 World Fencing Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Allround_Speed_Skating_Championships" title="2001 World Allround Speed Skating Championships">2001 World Allround Speed Skating Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Interuniversity_Games" title="2008 World Interuniversity Games">2008 World Interuniversity Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Modern_Pentathlon_Championships" title="2008 World Modern Pentathlon Championships">2008 World Modern Pentathlon Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_ITU_World_Championship_Series" title="2010 ITU World Championship Series">2010 ITU World Championship Series</a>, 2011 <a href="/wiki/IIHF_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="IIHF World Championship">IIHF World Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Fencing_Championships" title="2013 World Fencing Championships">2013 World Fencing Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Wrestling_Championships" title="2013 World Wrestling Championships">2013 World Wrestling Championships</a>, 2014 <a href="/wiki/World_Masters_Athletics_Championships" title="World Masters Athletics Championships">World Masters Athletics Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="2017 World Aquatics Championships">2017 World Aquatics Championships</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Judo_Championships" title="2017 World Judo Championships">2017 World Judo Championships</a>, only in the last two decade. Besides these, Hungary was the home of many European-level tournaments, like <a href="/wiki/2006_European_Aquatics_Championships" title="2006 European Aquatics Championships">2006 European Aquatics Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_European_Aquatics_Championships" title="2010 European Aquatics Championships">2010 European Aquatics Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Judo_Championships" title="2013 European Judo Championships">2013 European Judo Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Karate_Championships" title="2013 European Karate Championships">2013 European Karate Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_European_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 European Rhythmic Gymnastics Championships">2017 European Rhythmic Gymnastics Championship</a> and will be the host of 4 matches in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>, which will be held in the 67,889-seat new <a href="/wiki/Multi-purpose_stadium" title="Multi-purpose stadium">multi-purpose</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Pusk%C3%A1s_Ferenc_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="New Puskás Ferenc Stadium">Puskás Ferenc Stadium</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="Hungarian Grand Prix">Hungarian Grand Prix</a> in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> has been held at the <a href="/wiki/Hungaroring" title="Hungaroring">Hungaroring</a> just outside <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, which circuit has <a href="/wiki/FIA" class="mw-redirect" title="FIA">FIA</a> Grade 1 license.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup> Since 1986, the race has been a round of the <a href="/wiki/FIA" class="mw-redirect" title="FIA">FIA</a> <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> World Championship. At the <a href="/wiki/2013_Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="2013 Hungarian Grand Prix">2013 Hungarian Grand Prix</a>, it was confirmed that Hungary will continue to host a Formula 1 race until 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup> The track was completely resurfaced for the first time in early 2016, and it was announced the Grand Prix's deal was extended for a further five years, until 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a> is also a popular and successful sport in Hungary, the Hungarian players are the 10th most powerful overall on the ranking of <a href="/wiki/World_Chess_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="World Chess Federation">World Chess Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[252]</a></sup> There are about 54 <a href="/wiki/Grandmaster_(chess)" title="Grandmaster (chess)">Grandmasters</a> and 118 <a href="/wiki/International_Masters" class="mw-redirect" title="International Masters">International Masters</a> in Hungary, which is more than in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> or <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. World top junior player is the Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Rich%C3%A1rd_Rapport" title="Richárd Rapport">Richárd Rapport</a> currently on the <a href="/wiki/FIDE_World_Rankings" class="mw-redirect" title="FIDE World Rankings">FIDE World Rankings</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Judit_Polg%C3%A1r" title="Judit Polgár">Judit Polgár</a> generally considered the <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_chess#Strength" title="Glossary of chess">strongest</a> female chess player of all time. Some of the world's best <a href="/wiki/Sabre_(fencing)" title="Sabre (fencing)">sabre</a> athletes have historically also hailed from Hungary,<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[254]</a></sup> and in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Hungary_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Hungary men's national ice hockey team">Hungary men's national ice hockey team</a> qualified for their first <a href="/wiki/IIHF_World_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="IIHF World Championships">IIHF World Championship</a>, in 2015, they qualified for their second World Championship in the top division. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Hungary" title="Football in Hungary">Football in Hungary</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg/170px-Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg/255px-Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg/340px-Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2399" data-file-height="3650"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s" title="Ferenc Puskás">Ferenc Puskás</a>, the best goalscorer of the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Pusk%C3%A1s_Award" title="FIFA Puskás Award">FIFA Puskás Award</a> named after him
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hungary has won three Olympic football titles, finished runners-up in the <a href="/wiki/1938_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1938 FIFA World Cup">1938</a> and <a href="/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1954 FIFA World Cup">1954 FIFA World Cups</a>, and third in <a href="/wiki/1964_European_Nations%27_Cup" title="1964 European Nations' Cup">Euro 1964</a>. Hungary revolutionised the sport in the 1950s, laying the tactical fundamentals of <a href="/wiki/Total_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Total football">total football</a> and dominating international football with the <a href="/wiki/Magical_Magyars" class="mw-redirect" title="Magical Magyars"><i>Aranycsapat</i></a> ("Golden Team"), which included <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s" title="Ferenc Puskás">Ferenc Puskás</a>, top goalscorer of the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-FIFA_benefit_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA_benefit-256">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spanish_obit_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanish_obit-257">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Puskás_auction_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puskás_auction-258">[257]</a></sup> to whom FIFA dedicated<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[258]</a></sup> its newest award, the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA Ferenc Puskás Award">Puskás Award</a>. The side of that era has the second <a href="/wiki/World_Football_Elo_Ratings#All-time_highest_ratings" title="World Football Elo Ratings">all-time highest Football Elo Ranking in the world</a>, with 2166, and one of the longest undefeated runs in football history, remaining unbeaten in 31 games spanning more than four years.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The post-golden age decades saw a gradually weakening Hungary, though recently there is renewal in all aspects. The Hungarian Children's Football Federation was founded in 2008, as youth development thrives. For the first time in Hungarian football's history, they hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Futsal_Championship" title="2010 UEFA Futsal Championship">2010 UEFA Futsal Championship</a> in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Debrecen" title="Debrecen">Debrecen</a>, the first time the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Football_Federation" title="Hungarian Football Federation">MLSZ</a> staged a <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> finals tournament. Also, the national teams have produced some surprise successes such as beating <a href="/wiki/Euro_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a> 3–2<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[260]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> 3–1.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> Hungary won <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_Group_F" title="UEFA Euro 2016 Group F">Group F</a> and were eventually defeated in the round of 16. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFBernstein2003" class="citation news cs1">Bernstein, Richard (9 August 2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9B07E3D91531F93AA3575BC0A9659C8B63&amp;pagewanted=2">"East on the Danube: Hungary's Tragic Century"</a>. <i>The New York Times</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">15 March</span> 2008</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+New+York+Times&amp;rft.atitle=East+on+the+Danube%3A+Hungary%27s+Tragic+Century&amp;rft.date=2003-08-09&amp;rft.aulast=Bernstein&amp;rft.aufirst=Richard&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fquery.nytimes.com%2Fgst%2Ffullpage.html%3Fres%3D9B07E3D91531F93AA3575BC0A9659C8B63%26pagewanted%3D2&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHungary" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130_87-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-J._Lee_Ready_1995_page_130_87-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">J. Lee Ready (1995), <i>World War Two. Nation by Nation</i>, London, Cassell, page 130. 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-85409-290-1" title="Special:BookSources/1-85409-290-1">1-85409-290-1</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-bbc-no-warning-to-hungary-jews-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-bbc-no-warning-to-hungary-jews_88-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFMike_Thomson2012" class="citation web cs1">Mike Thomson (13 November 2012). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-20267659">"Could the BBC have done more to help Hungarian Jews?"</a>. BBC (British broadcasting service). <q>the BBC broadcast every day, giving updates on the war, general news and opinion pieces on Hungarian politics. But among all these broadcasts, there were crucial things that were not being said, things that might have warned thousands of Hungarian Jews of the horrors to come in the event of German occupation. A memo setting out policy for the BBC Hungarian Service in 1942 states: "We shouldn't mention the Jews at all". By 1943, the BBC Polish Service was broadcasting the exterminations. And yet his policy of silence on the Jews was followed until the German invasion in March 1944. After the tanks rolled in, the Hungarian Service did then broadcast warnings. But by then it was too late "Many Hungarian Jews who survived the deportations claimed that they had not been informed by their leaders, that no one had told them. But there's plenty of evidence that they could have known," said David Cesarani, professor of history at Royal Holloway, University of London.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Could+the+BBC+have+done+more+to+help+Hungarian+Jews%3F&amp;rft.pub=BBC+%28British+broadcasting+service%29&amp;rft.date=2012-11-13&amp;rft.au=Mike+Thomson&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.co.uk%2Fnews%2Fworld-europe-20267659&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHungary" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">

         <li id="cite_note-225"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-225">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mek.oszk.hu/02100/02172/html/index.html">Szabolcsi</a> Although the Hungarian upper class has long had cultural and political connections with the rest of Europe, leading to an influx of European musical ideas, the rural peasants maintained their own traditions such that by the end of the 19th century Hungarian composers could draw on rural peasant music to (re)create a Hungarian classical style. For example, <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Bart%C3%B3k" title="Béla Bartók">Béla Bartók</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zolt%C3%A1n_Kod%C3%A1ly" title="Zoltán Kodály">Zoltán Kodály</a>, two of Hungary's most famous composers, are known for using folk themes in their own music.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-226"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-226">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Szalipszki, p. 12<br>Refers to the country as "widely considered" to be a "home of music".</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Broughton-227"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Broughton_227-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Broughton, pp. 159–167</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-228"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-228">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Szabolcsi, <i>The Specific Conditions of Hungarian Musical Development</i><br>"Every experiment, made from Hungarian antecedents and on Hungarian soil, to create a conscious musical culture (music written by composers, as different from folk music), had instinctively or consciously striven to develop widely and universally the musical world of the folk song. Folk poetry and folk music were deeply embedded in the collective Hungarian people's culture, and this unity did not cease to be effective even when it was given from and expression by individual creative artists, performers and poets."</span> </li>

                  <div class="plainlist">
                   <ul>
                    <li><sup>1</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li>
                    <li><sup>2</sup> Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.</li>
                   </ul>
                  </div>
                 </div></td>
               </tr>
              </tbody>
             </table>
            </div>
